et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille;	and the smell of the oil inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm when boiling, as it is distilled into the ear.
et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	and be careful that it is not too cold, because the medicine would not be very good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear obstruction
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles;	No child is born without some ear problems.
et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir;	and this also happens to some people due to injury of the wound, or a foreign body inside the ear, and this injury comes only once in the ear, if one cannot see it;
et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	and never comes out without breaking the bone, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil;	Therefore, that which comes in the front, if one cannot see it, is a difficult healing in many positions, and in this, it is necessary that you put the ear with the bad side to the sun;
et regarde dedens:	and look inside:
se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	if you see the opacification, if the work has this entire span of why it is there:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille;	And let the forceps be applied evenly on both sides, front and back, so that it does not pierce the ear.
se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	If the discharge is from the ear or the ear canal, if you have fine forceps and gently cover it, until the wax is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wound is in the front of the ear, take a fine knife and lightly heat it over the fire, then place it on the bone of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille;	If you feel the discharge that causes the patient to have a grating sensation in the ear, slightly pierce it, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear.
puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	Then put a tent according to the size of the perforation in the ear, and tie it with an Egyptian knot.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet;	Do not do anything until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moor it in sharp rose, and powder with broken glass vitrified.
et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And if you see the ear swelling, it is advisable to remove the tent and move another tent moored in sharp rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as he is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if there is a flow of blood, dip an sponge and wrap it in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the blood flow which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the char of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines;	This is the eyelid that comes in papers from the eyes when they are wet and dry, if it is advisable to extend them with forceps and tweezers, and the cover of a sponge from its roots.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Then apply the acidic vinegar to the joint.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues;	And if without skin, then cauterize with a thin, pointed needle cauterizer, and the cauterizer after incision is better.
et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines;	And many times they recur, but nothing remains from their roots.
et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz;	Many times come from the eyes things that seem like grains in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "grandine", and is an assembly of large moisture above and below.
li ovraiges est telz:	The work is such as follows:
pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir;	If the shoulder moves back and forth, it is a simple matter to know;
fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Then make the incision wide, then scrape each part lightly, then take it with pincers and bandage.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide;	If you do not cover it with a small piece of paper, it will not hurt the patient.
et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	And if the wound is large, stitch it together and treat it until it is healed.
et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	And if it is small, do not make any force, for the pain will return quickly and cause harm.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre;	And if the large bone is falling downwards into the depth of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the large bone in some pinchers, and hold and press it from both sides.
et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien;	and if the paper is separated by the incision, it does not matter.
et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	and when the large bone is cut, pour some oil of vinegar on it, and cure the limb from which it was removed until the hairs are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz;	Exinach is a grease that is injected into the papers above, and it has more effect on children than adults, and hurts their eyes greatly, and they vomit in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears gather in their eyes.
et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	and because they lie on their faces adhered, and sleep on them, and their papers are soaked with moisture that inflames and irritates the skin which opens in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the limb to its place and feel the bone slipping between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain;	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs put their head on your healthy one;
et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li;	and then take a piece of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the oil from each part, then put it on him.
et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle;	and press with your two fingers on one side and the other, so that the oil is gathered in the circle.
puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne;	Then make a cut in the middle of the moisture using a sharp spatula, and it should not be larger than the wound made during the opening of the vein.
et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach;	And make a cut in the skin until you reach the extraction.
et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And in many positions, extraction comes from the cut, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars;	Extract the whole piece with a cloth wrapped around your fingers, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out.
et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	And make sure you do not insert it into the cut, that you do not come to the whole spatula just to the oil, that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere;	And if it does not open at the beginning of the incision, then sharply cut the incision lightly until it opens.
puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	Then extract it as we have said, then gently wipe the cloths in vinegar and water, and place on the limb, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break the cloth and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the abscess that is swollen, then the healer should apply wet compresses until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz;	When hairs are plucked out other than by nature, and are awakened, they harm the eyes, and bring on diseases such as tears and softening of the papers and cornea, until it is caused by the destruction of the eyes.
et est li cure selonc IIII manieres:	And there are four ways of treatment:
ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	For the fire cauterization together with fire, or by medicine according to what it is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre;	It is necessary that you put the head of the dislocated joint in your hand, then turn the paper of oil to your right hand.
s’elle est convertie, c’est boin;	If it is turned, it is good.
se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus;	If not, if you prick with a needle at the end of each thread above.
et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur;	And let it be either on the edge of the paper or where the hair grows from these hairs, and pull the thread above the entire paper, and turn to the razor.
puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit;	then cut in the part outside the paper, outside the hairs, removing all the skin, from the large thigh to the small one.
puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	then extract the thread, and place outside the paper a small tent of cotton and linen, then above the paper a figure of an envelope, like the fullness of mercury, and all the while it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you see lifted the paper which is divided into all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie;	And if to the thread that has business, one covers great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened;
puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit;	then make a cut across all the skin on the two lines you have marked, and begin from the large thigh down to small.
et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute;	and let one of the cuts near the hairs at the base of the large thigh, then push the knife into one of the two corners of the knee, then scrape the skin off entirely.
puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce;	then sew the two lips together with a needle and thread of fine silk, and stop the bleeding, and make sure the excess hair is above the stitches on all parts that are sticky, if you see this happening.
et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII;	and if not, then do not worry about it, then leave the stitches and the thread for three days or four.
puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	Then treat the wound with dry and constricting things, for the paper will revive at the moment of the wound and gather with it, but the sewing is broken (as the ancients said), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere:	And if in another way:
et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and you shape the paper into a form that is as like the mold of wax as we have told, at three fingerbreadths thick, according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cover the wound with a bandage evenly according to the form that is there:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure;	And if you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or a thread that has one strand, and put it into the figure;
et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment;	et boute I autre fil delez lou grand larmier, et lou seconde fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les fils igalment.
puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then evenly lift your hand, and lift all the skin above where you have sewn, as we have told you, then gather the two lips of the wound by sewing, and treat it until it is healed.
et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with plaster and similar soothing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit:	and never has it happened that the hair of the stone is converted:
si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision;	if you should use what we have said about incision.
mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme:	The treatment of wounds is as follows:
et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est;	and you should convert the paper and the fence inside according to what I have said, and then make two wounds by art, and two thin lines as long as the paper and the width of the space is;
et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz;	and take care of the two parts where you hold the threads;
puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment;	then assemble them subtly above what lies over the paper of the oil, and strain the two wounds from the two parts formed;
et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	and he leaves it thus for several days, and the skin that is stretched will die, rot, and putrefy, and will fall off from it.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	If it takes too long, then the copper (cauterizing instrument) must be used with force, and cure until it is healed.
et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil;	And when the wound has been closed, and if paper has been lifted from it, and the hairs will not grow back.
et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	And this is the shape of the two needles that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil;	The work is such that you grip a thin needle, and pull the silk thread soft and thin;
puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc;	Then gently gather the heads and place them one by one, and let the hair grow a palm's length long.
puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil;	Then order the other hair in a quick hunt of silk thread briefly, and do not let the heads touch the thread.
puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain;	Then place the misaligned heads on your clean side.
et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil;	And let the work be done in the shade so that the work is not spoiled, for it is a delicate and small work, then push the needle through the entire hair at its base pricked, and pierce it into the paper gently until you remove it above the natural hair;
puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors;	Then shave the hair up to the chest, and cut off the hair in the chest, if there is one or two or three or more.
puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	Then shave your hand until the hair comes out all over the chest, with the natural hair on the paper.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil;	And if the chest is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then shave the chest to the very end, as far as you have ordered, until the chest comes out completely and you can see through the oil.
adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus;	Then shave the chest and the hair, and close the oil and leave it for two or three days, until the hair grows back in its place and grows on top.
et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the hairs are small, accompany them with long hair from sheep, and elevate it with the one you leave, until they are lengthened and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purity of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres:	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the "porridge," comes in the oil, there are two ways:
l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	One natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs by a wound, or a cut, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And the way of the work in it is that you break that seal, and dry the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed.
et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And you should only use in its care things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere;	For if you do this, the disease will become worse than before.
mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic;	but I work on things that are softening, such as fenugreek.
et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	and the strong herbs and seeds of flax be cooked, and the ointment of yarrow dissolved in any of the oils, and it is wrapped in a tent, and this is the cure for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant;	And the treasures of your cure are such that you should take care not to spoil it according to its former form.
et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And these works that we have said are not other than to prevent this disease from returning according to its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil which comes in the jar
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is dislocated, which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans;	Accidents come from wounds, cuts, burns, and similar things.
et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char;	And the method of the work is such that you grasp a needle with a double thread, and place it in the chair, and make it pierce from the right arm to the left, so that the thread comes out at two points on the chair.
puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Then the chair is above all the needle, and the cloth is wide enough to cover it.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin;	And if the paper shape returns according to what is needed, it is good.
se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere;	If not, take the razor and place it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two more cuts inside the paper.
et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»;	and let the two cuts of the two corners of the incision that you have made be such that when they are assembled, that the figure is as it should be, like the shape of a letter that has not been Greek.
puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne;	then take that char, according to the amount that its cost is away from it, of what is taught on paper, then add the two parts together, and stitch them with a thread of linen.
puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then take care of what we have said about the medicines that soften and the bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant;	And if the illness comes from a cut or stitching or cauterization, then it is necessary that you make a plain incision away from the hairs of the paper, and according to what is above.
puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit;	then carefully place between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said.
et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil;	and one should perform the work according to the form of the disease, as it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters compare all possible means to how they can make the figure return to its natural shape.
et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	and the bones themselves, according to what is needed for work and tools in many positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut;	When this glue is done by hand in a somewhat manner that the paper above is soaked with the white of oil, and cannot move or do its natural workings, then it is necessary that you bring the point of a razor outside the paper, and tie it on top.
et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil;	and it is used with pins, until you copy what is hard at the subtle space, which should not be too sharp nor too blunt, so that the pain cannot suffer that the space is too sharp or blinds the oil.
et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil;	and your incision should be lightly scraped off that assembly, so that the paper reverts according to its natural form.
et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere;	and it is all clean that assembly, and never in the oil acid salty, and lift from acid sweet, and of colloid.
puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef;	then put between the paper and the oil a linen tent, and put on the oil wool ground in abundance of urine.
et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the first day, use a cold compress and unclean things until healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres:	There are two ways to treat the joint:
elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om;	The first way is when the joint is like a hard, painful spasm, and the other way is not nerve-related but resembles frozen moisture, so that when touched with iron and heated with pincers, it cannot be moved.
et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Both ways start near the great thigh bone and grow slowly until they cover the entire eye and light, and all movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz;	And the way of the incision is that the hairs put their head in your clean place, then they work the eyes.
et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus;	and gently hold the paper to your hand, then bend the nail with small force, and extend it above;
puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort;	then take a needle, and put horsehair, or sheep's wool, or beef fat, and thread it tightly;
et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement;	and double the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and push the entire needle through, and tie the nail with a thread and extend it above, and scrape all the hair from the side of the nail that leads to the pearl and silk to the skin just below the arm, then cut the remaining in the root of the arm at every subtle space and with small forces, and leave the natural bend of the arm, so that by the incision, tears do not usually come out;
et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit;	and never once has the joint remained out of place alone, but rather as we have said.
puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	then the skin is all the soft tissue that gives shape to this.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie;	And be careful that the soft tissue does not touch the fascia and tear it, and that the bone is not pierced.
et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	and after the incision pour some ground black pepper into the oil, and a poultice made of linen, and leave it just above the other side.
puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply the appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines;	and if the joint is not nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the joints cannot enter, often this resemblance of a dislocation from medicine.
et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	and they grow as I have described in the section, and if you see them covered, then oil the hair with the bad one, and take the sharp instrument lightly, quickly according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor;	and gently rub the joint above, and if you see that it does not soften and the skin is close, then distill from your mouth into the oil mixture made of litharge and red wax and silk broth, and stifle the oil with the other one;
puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	then begin the other work according to this same work, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the oil, as with an abscess, then milk, and cure first the abscess until it is healed, then proceed with the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne;	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm appears black in the oil due to great harm, then suspend it at the end, and cover a part of it and not all at once, so that tears do not come.
puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	then distill in the oil red chalices which are made of litargire.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that comes out above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste;	Some men are born with no red hair, and cover the prunelle and hold it up on the papers and turn it to the back, and it seems like a baluster rose.
et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force;	and the work is such that the hairs put their heads in your clean, then work those, and hold all that hair with convenient bends for this, and support it at force.
puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige;	Then shave the first chapiter, and go through everything shaving to the end, and be careful not to cut the oil in the work.
et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	And it should be the same incision of the span that we have mentioned in the incision of the nail and with small forces to take out the base, as it forms after this chapter shows.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut;	And when the incision is completed and all the chapter is taken out, use oil of sulfur or you distill red wine and similar corrosive medicines, and put it on the oil with a piece of cotton with absinth, so that it is secure against pus.
et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut;	and if there is nothing delayed, and the swelling does not subside, and you doubt an abscess, leave the oil and treat the abscess with soothing remedies.
puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	then return to your work until it is healed, and thus make certain that the char is set in oil by this means.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil;	But always it is necessary that you apply a weak remedy of the natural way;
et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer;	and of the accidental way, in ironwork;
et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	red veins that are covered over the eye, and they harm the view and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel;	The first task is therefore to examine the patient's eyes, to see if they are open or closed, and there is no other disease besides this one.
adonques le coil en teil maniere:	Therefore, examine the patient in this manner:
comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Instruct the patient to place their head in your hand, then gently stretch the joints at all angles according to their wisdom, and let the subtle joints be doubled in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they should be done twice a day, gradually increasing in intensity according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil;	Then examine the patient's joints gently, and squeeze the blood out after each time until you can remove them from the eye.
et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes;	Be careful not to pierce the eye with sharp objects, and perform this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not cause any harm to the joints.
et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And when you have done this, if you distill green and red wine into the oil to corrupt what is remaining underneath.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you cannot collect all the wine in that hour, then make a poultice on the oil of things to ease the pain of the eyes, and let it sit for some time until the pain is eased and it is ensured that there is no abscess, then restart according to this method as long as it is not healed;
et c’est li forme des forces:	and this is the form of the force:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the oil fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule:	The master named "Aristarchus" made a fistula:
quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	When you cure it with fire and medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then apply the same thing that you did above the abscess, where it should die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme;	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then the instrument of all that is in this form;
et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	and is called "sharp chisel", and it is made of iron into the form of a chisel, and it is pointed as a lime if it is in this present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese;	And place it above the flesh of the bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that that corruption is removed;
et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	and do not do it again, then restore the flesh of healing drying agents.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez;	if the wound is sound, and the flesh has grown, and the body of the bone is sound, and it remains thus for forty days, and it does not remove and is not displaced, and no bad accidents come, then it is healed;
se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme:	If not, there is no other method than to bring the fistula to the point of the nose according to this form:
et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	and then you should discover the bone again with iron and medicines, and when it is discovered take the forehead according to this form, and let the patient's iron be at three angles, and the fuse should be thinned down to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif;	then put it above the bone of the arm, and keep your hand away from the oil for a moment, then turn the whole forehead until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain as if it comes from the inside if he keeps his hand on his nose;
et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif;	and when the bone of medicine is dried, as I have shown you, and when the child grows and hardens the bones, then the matter goes to the knee.
si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	It is a lighter matter for the joint.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide;	When the eyes are widely open and not disturbed or drowsy, it is necessary to hold the joint.
puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz;	Then the healthy one, then apply leeches or a hot iron to draw out the poison, then place on the oil that has been made with acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and strain the oil, and apply the ointment with bandages and cloths;
et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier;	and the manner of the cloths is such that you grasp cloths that are sufficiently soft, and fold each one into four, and then place one on top of the other according to the quantity that they have need of.
puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir;	then strain through a cloth made of linen firmly, and restart the suction to draw without harming.
puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout;	then remove the suctions and let the oil remain strained day and night, and if the joints are dislocated, it is necessary that you strain it greatly.
puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin;	then remove the joint after the day and night, and if you see the oil return, it is good.
se ce non;	if not
si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the bandages and the cloths and the linen and the suction devices are not clean until they are healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The breaking of a silk cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir;	When disruptions come in the woven cloth, then open, and come strong like the grain of resin, and is spreadable to see.
adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier;	then if you see the cloth covered, the work is such that you put a needle in the root of the part below this above, then put another needle where the double thread of the arm part is.
et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition;	and make it pierce, and let the first needle according to the arrangement.
puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef;	then copper the joint with a doubled and tied piece of cloth, and strain it well, then remove the needle and put some soft marrow on the wound in plenty.
et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee;	and leave it until the thread heals with the wound, then care for the oil of things that comfort until the wound is healed.
et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and never strain the wound by any piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost;	And if they appear greatly, then pierce the thin needle that comes from under the oil, and wick away the moisture and descend on the hairs, and enter immediately.
puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then I removed it until it was healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the front of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue;	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is nothing more than a bowel that is gathered in the oil, resembling a sharp downward point, and it is not a sharp point.
et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz;	And the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on the seat with their back straight, then take the chief between your hands from the two parts, and move it until you see the bowel come out above to your eyes.
puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit;	Then let it be removed, and do not descend and it should be dismantled in the light, and see the things as they were.
et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	And if they do not dislocate, it is sharp, and if they do not descend from the bow, it is not as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse;	If you place the pain between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it under the eye, by the continuation of the conjunctiva with the eyelid and the eyebrow, until the bow is released.
et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when it is released, distill in the hot, sharp oil mixed with honey, or sharp or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the hot oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier;	We have similarities of waters in the division, and what is necessary to pierce.
si en oevre selonc la santeit.	if in work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort;	You must make the misaligned bone between your crossed hands, outside of the light for the sun, and the sound and stretched very tight.
puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres;	Then put the paper of oil to your right hand if the eyes are right, or to your left hand if the eyes are left.
puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre;	Then take in your right hand if the eyes are right, or in your left hand if the eyes are left, the instrument called "almagda".
puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide;	Then place the tip of the instrument on the crown by the thickness of a ring in the small bone of the elbow, then drive the instrument which is called «almagda» virtuously, and tremble your hand until it pierces through the small bone of the elbow, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing.
et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour;	And it is appropriate that the measure of the path of almagda be at the forepart of the measure of the space that is from the prunella to the end of the nostril.
et c’est li corone de l’oil;	And this is the crown of the oil.
si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	If you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the canvas cloth, then place the instrument next to it where the sharp is, then express it out one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he is now sharp-sighted, then he sees the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc;	After a short rest, and if the pain increases again, use the second method. Place the forceps with the instrument, and when it is securely gripped and does not move, gently rotate your hand back and forth.
et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	Then apply a little force with the string gem, and let it go inside the vein.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in its place the oil steeped or ground with rose oil and an abundance of honey, and bind it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on it with an abundance of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the arrowhead cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you use the tool called "alberit", of which this is the form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit;	And then only pierce the connective tissue, and do not go too far in front, but make the cut gently, then use the forceps as we have said.
et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous;	And at the completion of the work, compare the patient's sleep with the darkness that occurs, in which he sleeps on his back in the darkened room.
et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor;	and it is necessary to avoid all movements, and take light foods, and not move the head to the right or left, and it should be tied according to its position just after the injury.
puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor;	then the reset it in this very dark house, and examine its view, and let see some things, and then put the chain just after the seventh day.
et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	and it is necessary that you do this in the early hours of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise the head, because the sharp pain quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme;	if abscesses come, then you reset the oil before the seventh day, and it is necessary to raise the head which alleviates the abscess.
et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	And when it is calm, remove the bandage and place it on its face again to cover any opening, and let it stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas;	Then slowly leave the house and turn into your own home;
et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	and let no one interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens;	Some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country people used to do something called "almagda perciet," which is like the aigue, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read about it in the books of the ancients;
et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And by chance, this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie;	And these are the similar forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see them as such;
et soient d’arain proprement:	and they are purely rain.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And they are the heads of those from this same subtlety, and the others in three angles awake.
de la char sor le neis	for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez;	Never born or born different charcoals, of which there are some that seem like scorpions at the bottom of the feet;
et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	and if there are such and he has enhanced char of dark color, and if he has charcoal of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In that case of these charcoals which is good, and not enhanced, it is appropriate to make the pain between your hands against the sun;
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	and clean his nostrils, and pour water into those holes, and remove them;
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	so that you can hold it with a fine, sharp needle until you know that the arrow is completely out.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if there is nothing that can be removed with a fine, delicate instrument, then open it with all the sharp tools until nothing remains.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if you do not see, or an abscess forms, then treat it as it should be;
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize it until the wound is clean and all the arrows are removed, then pour in salt water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If the neck is injured, and moisture comes into the palace, cut it open to see if it is healthy;
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, see if there is a fracture in the bone above, because the instruments do not come out to cut:
adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins;	therefore it is necessary that you bring a thin wire, and hold it with your hands, and put space between each nut as needed or less;
et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche;	and put the bad teeth of the wire into the neck at a low angle, and pull it out until it comes out through the neck inside the mouth;
et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire;	and often do so to children at schools, and it is an easy thing for those who wish to do it.
puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	Then hold the head that comes from the neck in one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and alternate between them as we have done before.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant;	Do this until you clean that cloth, then draw the child's tongue out, soak the blood, and remove the thread in an Egyptian manner, and put it back in the same way as before.
fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char;	Do this three times or more, until the incisions have eaten away all that remains of the cloth.
et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use;	Then place or remove a splint as needed for several days until they are healed, and if they need to use medicines, then do so.
et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	This is the shape of the instrument used to purge the head, where one distills the oils and medicines that are placed inside.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi;	And it should be of silver or tin, shaped like an open lamp, such as a cane, and use it in the same way.
et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief;	And if you see, then make a closed cane, and the instrument is used to purge the head.
et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should have a handle at the top to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	for the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder;	Frequently, a disease is born at the head of the neck, which is called "telul", and grows and becomes large over time, becoming such that it is difficult to see.
et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant;	And for this reason, you should cover it at the beginning, and apply the entire bone, then place the heat or burning medicine on the limb.
et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens:	And if it is delayed in covering until it becomes large, then take heed whether it is hard, of poor color, and without sensation:
si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide;	if you do not touch it with iron because these are buried abscesses, for when it is covered, great harm comes to the pain.
et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	and if it is an abscess, touch it gently, not with hot water, and you will see how you can cover it all, if you remove the pain and the cover without fear, and cure the limb of things that are tight and restrictive.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut off and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	that remedies for continuing come in one of these cartilages, and is of little use, because in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc;	Then it is necessary to look at the wound if it is fresh with all its blood;
et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply the two lips to a seam, then cure it until it is healed.
et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet;	and if the lips are already scarred on one side and the other, then it is necessary to scrape all the parts of their edge until they heal, then assemble the two lips to a seam, and hold it, and powder with powder of dragon's blood, and broken incense.
et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Put powders on top of the wound, using a strong or other adhesive plaster, and leave it until it heals through it, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution:	The manner of the stitching is such that you assemble the solution:
ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre;	or by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly;
ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant;	To some people there are within the lips abscesses that are hard and large, like grains, and smaller and larger;
adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie;	therefore it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut into each one, and take with forceps and cover in each part;
puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	then fill the wound after the incision of broken glass, until the wound is clean.
et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then apply a bandage to the wound, and treat the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the crown of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»;	Often teeth grow above the gums, which the ancients called "albulus".
si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc;	if it is necessary that you support it with pincers, and cover its root, and let the blood or pus out.
puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives;	then apply glass powder broken, or other astringent and desiccating powders;
et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize:	and if that tooth returns after the incision, and often happens, then cover it again, and cauterize.
si ne revient mie aprés le cautere;	if it does not return even after the cauterization;
et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	and these are the forms of instruments to cover.
des sordens	of the deaf
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres;	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, scars that are ugly and sharp;
et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant;	and sometimes they are the black and yellow and green teeth, until the corruption comes to the gum, and are the stinking teeth.
si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien;	if it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands, and its roots are in your holy one, and extract the teeth or the scars that appear, until nothing remains.
et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees;	and thus make of the black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are removed;
et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin;	and if it has taken out what is at the first layer, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis;	if not, start again from the second layer and the third, until you have removed everything.
et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens;	and clean the teeth of various forms of instruments to remove, according to what the operation demonstrates, because the razor that is removed from between the teeth has other shapes than the one that is removed from between the teeth.
et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire;	When you are treating a tooth for pain, do not delay in pulling it as soon as possible, for one should not do this to everyone.
car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	for it is a very high substance, so there is no excuse for not pulling it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the tooth is painful and must be pulled, then you should be certain of the tooth breaking.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent;	Often the pain of the misaligned joint is relieved, and one should ensure that it is a holy tooth, and pull out the good tooth.
et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors;	and one should not leave it until the pain is relieved, as long as the evil remains, for we have already done this to these sinners.
et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars;	And when you are certain of the tooth that is hurting, it is necessary that you cauterize around the tooth on all sides. with a strong burning agent to protect the gum from all parts.
puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles;	Then move the joint to its proper place or use thin needles at the first point and then another, until it is properly dislocated, then firmly secure the needles.
et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	And if the painful joint is in your knee, keep it still so it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not jump back into place, take any of these instruments and gently tap on each part lightly, and then shake as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont;	And if the joint is dense and swollen, then it is necessary to fill it with cloths where the pus is.
et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre;	And if the thin needles are delicately held, so they do not break when being pulled out.
et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And it is necessary to carefully observe around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, and re-insert it with more pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit;	And be careful that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant scribes, who by their haste and boldness break everything at once, and never correct what we have told.
mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut;	but bring forth everything once by the cunning of this great disease for the roots that they delay, or for the chariot that they break, as we have often seen.
et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil;	and when the tooth is drawn, wash the mouth with wine or with oil and salt.
et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet;	and if blood flows and it often does, use the mouth with broken glass wine.
et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	If it does not improve, then cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent;	The forms of the instruments that one uses to move the first teeth should be long and pointed, and have large handles, so they do not bend when you pull out the tooth.
et ce sont les formes:	And these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick-bodied so they do not bend when you pull, and they should be made of well-made iron, and they should be sharp to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou II, tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne;	When the root remains in the tooth, it is necessary to place cotton moilliet on the tooth or II, until the tooth is softened, then break the forceps called "algefri," which are used to extract the tooth.
et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	And they should be made inside like a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, then it is necessary that you dig around the root of the whole chariot, and put the tool called «althali», that is, a spoon, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin;	And if it is also large and thick so that it does not break, and if its root jumps upwards, it is good.
se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If not, with all the instruments, of which the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if it helps, then use this tool that has two prongs, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the range of the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large needles, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont;	And this instrument is except that it cannot break, and sharp that many of the instruments of density are;
et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez;	and also other instruments, which are not counted as one.
et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and the wise masters subtly find their own instrument, according to what their work and the disease shows, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach the instrument for the diversity of the others and it has not broken the cart or the other bones, or it does not harm, if one seeks the instruments that one needs, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster;	And let them be large and well-gripping to hold the bone, that it not slip, but let him hold and remove.
et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	Then restore the limb to its proper position, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then cut off all this tool.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer:	When the tooth appears not in line with its natural position, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, then it is necessary to remove the tooth if it is not in the right place, and cannot be straightened or filed.
adonques lou raie;	Then cut off the root.
et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	and if it is stuck with the tooth, take this tool that has this shape, and it is similar to a small beak, and it should be made of iron, sharp on one side and smooth on the other.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper coin gently and slowly for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be lamed, then the lame part of a spoon like this is used:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles;	and it is also like the bill of the bird from which we make arrows;
et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece;	and in the bill of the tooth gently and slowly move it back and forth, so that it does not move until it breaks;
puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	then the flat end of it has no razor, and if the tooth is too sharp and it cuts the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth are locked
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut;	When the teeth in front are knocked out, whether by impact or falling, and the pain cannot be relieved by pressing on the gums to prevent them from chattering, and you treat them with restrictive medicines, it is not effective.
si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques;	if they need to be restricted with a gold thread, for the silver thread becomes green and rotten, but the gold never changes.
et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens;	and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth.
