et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part;	and if you see that the teeth are becoming loose, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the missing tooth between the other teeth, as many as there are, until you feel confident that the healthy tooth on the other side is secure.
puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point;	then reapply the bandage to the part where you began, and gently and carefully insert your hand, until it does not move.
et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	and let your finger be at the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue;	Then cut the thread into small pieces and use them to assemble, and put them between the healthy tooth and the tongue, so it does not bleed.
et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil;	Then leave it so tight as it can stay, and if it dislocates, or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread.
si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	If it stays and serves in this way throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the appearance of the crowning of the two healthy teeth, and the two missing ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit;	And when the tooth is knocked out, if it is put back into its place, bit by bit, as we have said;
et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	and does not interfere with it if it is not wise and painful, and never made the shape of a bone tooth of a goose, and put it back into its place where the defect is, and hold it as we have said, and wait and serve thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut open the vein of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi;	Never are these joints which come from the tongue or nature, that one should not thus make;
ou par accident de plaie soudee;	or by accident of a wound sewn.
et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue;	and the works are such that you work the mouth of the misaligned, and have his head in your safe, and relieve the tongue;
puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then cut the nerve of the arm, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and it is a sudden injury, then boil the herb and cut it lengthwise.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	And be careful that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is exposed;
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	And when you have done, lift the limb of vinegar and oil, or of cold water, then put out the tongue a tent of linen;
et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	and the taint the pain every night, that the limbs not stick together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet;	And if blood comes out, put glass powder on the wound;
et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu;	and if the bleeding does not stop, cauterize it with slow-burning fire, which is good for this.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	then use other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see that the wound is of black or dark color and hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, because it is a chancre.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	and if it is inclined to suppuration and there is moisture, then pour the liquid from a thin syringe on both sides and deliver it.
et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if it does not move in your work, place a piece of broken glass on top as long as it is soaked, then return to your work until you remove all the pus.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then lift the limb from the left and right, and treat other wounds until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	No one ever comes from within the throat, which are called "godath", and they are properly called the two mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful:
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if it is an abscess hard and small in size and of yellowish color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with a little iron, as it may cause the flow of blood;
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it be until it is soft, and then you will be able to part it, or it would break by itself;
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of white color and the root is thin, then you should prepare the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscesses are calm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then place the pain in front of the sun, and its head should be straight, and the work the mouth and the prince between his hands, and press the tongue away from all the instrument, because it is the shape;
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and let it be of silver or thin tin like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	if you press the tongue with this instrument, and see the abscess, take the needle and poke it into the amber, and trace it upward as much as you can;
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and take nothing with it from the threads, then cover the instrument with a cloth, of which this is the shape, which seems like a forceps;
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and all the prongs are bent, and one part is on the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or tin:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you have coping with pliers, of which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	and let it be called "trenchan" on one side, and "name" on the other:
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And when you have pulled out one of the splinters, pull out the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp pain with hot, sharp, and cold water, and if there is blood coming out, gargle with hot water, or use pounded green pomegranates, or mint leaves, and similar things, until the mouth is no longer stained.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then cure it until it is healed.
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And never do any other abscesses come out of the throat besides the two splinters, so pull them out in the same way as the two splinters must be pulled out.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was located within her throat, specifically a small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the condition that was choking her, and she could not eat or drink, and died if she remained like this for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had been filled with two handfuls of pus through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I therefore acted quickly, and pierced one of the sides, then removed the pus, and a large portion of blood.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I pierced the other side through the throat, and the work of the mouth and pressed her tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	After I had finished this work, I collected the remains in these abscesses, and took out a part of it, and did not finish until a small amount of blood was drawn.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	And thus the woman's throat was cut, and she began to drink vinegar and then wine, and did not stop cutting into this abscess by long stretches.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	And the abscesses returned to their place, and filled the skin that I had emptied, until it became very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	Therefore I advised her and cauterized it inside her throat.
ensi demora sens croistre;	Thus she did not grow without.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I leave these parts, and know only that God will do with them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When referring to the eye, and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	And if it is swollen and round, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help much, and you see that the chauffer's abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you should apply a poultice.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	And the one that is round and not long;
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is bloody or purple or black in color, then you should avoid the incision of the li.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its color and length, you should place the painful part in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then cut the wound in the uvula, and remove it, and wrap it with the second or third instrument that I have mentioned in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit;
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	because if you cover more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech;
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the second mandible, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is not alleviated by copper, then you should use an engine for cauterization of the sensitive pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterization is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And if the hairs put their head in your healthy hand, then press the tongue against the instrument we have said or in the chapter of cautery, and cut with a sharp, hot knife, so that it is not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And use the movement of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And have at the head a hair or olive oil, as with the movements of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine over the eye.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and the hairs lie flat on his chest, so that his saliva and muscle secretions from his mouth flow into the medicine inside, so it does not drip down his throat and into his belly.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	Then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it against the eye for a quarter of an hour, until you see that it is softened and the bitterness of the medicine is eased.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	And if you see it, take a piece of cloth and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cloth in the medicine, and blow the instrument into the cloth until the cloth is soaked with it.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	And do this often, until the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry and scab after four or five days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you are skilled in the art of restarting the cauterization, then restart it, and after the cauterization, apply a poultice of bread and butter around the eye, and clean what is around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be sure to use a sharp, cold knife, and treat with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, than cauterization;
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	If it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take camphor, hyssop, origanum, rue, chamomile, and veronica, and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and add oil, and boil;
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be well glued with strong earth, and inside the pot there should be an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And it should be of silver or tin, and one end of the instrument should be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the steam rises to the urethra through the ureter, until the urethra is dead.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	After that, it is often repeated until the urethra dries, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the onset of the abscess, because many things happen.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make steam except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not present, take a knife and place it within the head, so that the mouth does not have too much heat.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	for the knife does not cause much vapor to burden the mouth, and this is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	often it is asserted at the neck of bones or thorns of fish, or nothing.
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	therefore you should take what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and what you cannot see and is hidden in the neck, you should make vomit the evil immediately after the meat is cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	By chance, if the object is inserted through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the hairs swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and it sticks to the sponge thread, and then swallows it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when she comes to the belly, it will stick, and then pull out forcefully;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if she does not come out forcefully as we have said, take the instrument of plunger according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can more lightly enter the throat, and have the head raised high;
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that the whole does not come in, nor push the bone inside;
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and move it so that the hairs push the instrument, because it is often or the thing is there;
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the push goes down, or it pulls the instrument equally throughout, as long as it is full.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat opening
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	Never use the saliva, as I have said in the division, by the care of medicines;
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and when it does not profit you, then look at the throat of the hairs to the sun, then that you press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, trace it with a small needle or thin needles that are worthy of the eye.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if the eye does not hold, take a hair from the beard, and boil it in the patient's throat, then boil or move the hair with the iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the wounds bleed all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take full I of sharp cold water, and work the mouth, and pour it in the direction to swallow, and move it to your hand often.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if soon as he feels the cold, he spits.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if he does not spit as we have said, then fumigate the bad breath with sulfur, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the onion.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do it many times, for it will not last long.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	And the way of the fumigation is that you hold I pot where he has charcoal visible, and let it be covered with a linen cloth in the middle, and in that pierced is the sought instrument.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then you should use your fumigation, and the pain puts the head of the snake in their mouth, and closes their mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes to the nose.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the nose will now drip, and if it does not drip, then repeat the fumigation many times;
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers thirst, and eats salty and bitter things, and does not drink anything acidic;
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	then the patient will have the strength to be healed by this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the nose, so is, when it can be seen, resembles a crooked hook to enter into the throat;
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	And it resembles the beak of care, and there is sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot wear out.
et vez ci la forme:	and it has this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	There are many forms of abscesses, according to what memory comes after one and another in this book, and they vary in puncture and cut.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is in two ways that one is in its own form, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the arms or when they are at the sides.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the main abscesses are different from those that come from the foundation, and the abscesses of the shoulder joint are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if there are abscesses that one should not puncture, until the belly is complete according to its fulfillment.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if there are such as must be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die immediately upon completion, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come beyond joints, and it is left until it is surrounded by, perhaps because the ligament and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, by which this is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	When the abscess is beyond the main member, and if you delay piercing until it dies, it will harm the main member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	or it is beyond the foundation, if you pierce when it has died;
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it should not be pierced until the abscess is ripe for digestion, except that which is beyond the foundation, so that it does not putrefy and remain inside, and there comes a fistula.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is necessary to lance the pus from the abscess according to its completion, and this is when the pain is relieved, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and swelling, and the decrease in debility and easing of the main symptom of the abscess, and the other signs;
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	And it is necessary to make the incision higher or more dependent on the limb of the abscess, and where it opens most widely;
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and whether the incision is long or short, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places equally where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the affected member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the limb, it is best to leave the puncture until it is confirmed that digestion has been completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	If you were to pierce it before heaven, then the blood would flow out of it, and it would be stained with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	And perhaps they harden the lips and the deeply pierced ones of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured along the wide course of the blood vessel, according to what the limb has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	And it is necessary that you apply small abscesses, small incisions.
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	And in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the resemblance of the greatness of the abscess.
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	And if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover and bandage them.
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	When it has become as soft as a cloth, and is softened, then you should do as they do with bandages.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if there are some that are cut into three angles, and if there are some that are treated as if they were the back of a mirror, such as abscesses.
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if there are some where a round cut is made, and other cuts and shapes that cover.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them clearly.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	And when the abscess is large, and it has much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	Then stun the abscess just after the other day, then draw out nothing else.
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	Do this frequently with great force until the bow is completely broken.
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Even if the pain is of weak virtue, such as a woman carrying, or small children, or old decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never tremble once with the outflow of the pus, because perhaps the wounds might die, and you would not perish.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if you dry the wound, and look to see if the abscess wound is small;
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a boil, then soothe with linen or old cotton;
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is large abscesses, and there is much pus, then it is necessary that you put in each one a tent so that they come against each other;
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have cut into an abscess a part of the skin, and you have sewn it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or sawdust from a linen cloth to prevent moisture.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your work, apply sharp cold and wet cloths, and clean the wound, and place it on the affected area for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	and if the bleeding persists, and is not improved with government and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book are of no use, and if it is very painful, then you should place bandages and moistened cloths soaked in wine and oil on it.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	If it is in this state, and the limb is swollen, then it is necessary to apply fomentations of hot and cold cloths, or of wine and oil, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then drain the abscess, dry it, and treat it as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And one must know universally about the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	as I have told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and see the chapter.
des soros	from swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the head, and are of various kinds, like the lentils of a girl, and many such there are.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some and such as have moisture like chickens;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	And for those who are tough and have hard skin, there is no doubt if the artery does not move against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the cutting is such that you try all the instrument called "entromissoire", from which the form comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	If it contains moisture, then let it dry out from above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off anything that contains that moisture, for it will return if you leave anything.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	Then soak cotton in Egyptian oil, if present.
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	If not, use vinegar and honey, and apply to the wound, and leave it for the next day.
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And continue to do this until it is gone.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then restart the cotton, as before, the next day, and the third, until you are sure it will not remain for the night.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the wound of inflammation at this convenient time, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess holds much pus, then apply the poultice in this form, long and wide.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	And you should pour your urine, and the skin from all parts, and put all your care to draw out the cloth where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the artery makes it against you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also make an incision if it is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And if the incision is made over a pierced abscess and wet, it is lighter, for it is of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if any of these abscesses or wounds or they have no moisture, and of these were the abscess or wound that I copied or from an old woman;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, and could not break it.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if one had made any, they would have made just as much pain as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other abscesses coming or in the head, because those who come from the head and the roots of the ears, if the opening is always at the most dependent part of the head, to let out the pus;
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of hydroceles
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often have abscesses at the neck, and dislodge the testicles, and pierce, and sometimes come from other parts or the chest, and are very large, and are inflamed together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each boil is properly within its own side, like the abscess of the head, as we have said;
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and similar cases of these scrofulous swellings are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some evil ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that case which you see of good disposition at the touchstone, and resembling the color of the body, and motionless from every part and not attached to any nerve, blood vessel, or conduit, and not deeply penetrating;
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	if it is necessary to remove it from above, and scrape every part, and place the two lips of the wound together as soon as possible, if you have the skill, as we have said in abscesses of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	and pull it out little by little, and be sure that you do not remove the nerve or the vein, and that it is not deeply embedded, which the hands cannot escape, and do not expose too soon, before you cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you stop, put vinegar or some powders that coagulate blood into the wound, and hold the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and let it stay until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound is softened, and then begin to treat it.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	Then ask yourself if there are any small pustules remaining, and cut them out and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein at the root of the pustule, it is not recommended that you cut out that pustule at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through, without causing harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian oil, then apply the treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire abscess, it is necessary to gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, as there is no need for excess due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary to apply a covering to the root of it, and draw out the pus, and hold it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those abscesses that hold excessive pus should be punctured where it is most likely to bleed out;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and puncture it in such a way as the one previously mentioned, below, then apply bandages with oil and similar things, so that it does not corrupt what remains from the corruption;
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well bandaged, apply the treatment with healing charcoal until it is healed.
de squinance	of dislocation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and said of the throat cutter;
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen such a thing in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those who have tonsillitis, the part of the neck called "epiglottis" must be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and one cannot help with this, because all the veins and the source of the pain are in those who have abscesses deep in the mouth, or in the neck or in the armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the mouth, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it outside of three or four small incisions across, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision of the throat, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those people are suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no cartilage, and the gag is long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary to extend the skin of the neck all around, then cut the windpipe until it reaches the carotid artery.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the veins of blood, if you see anything, then cover the wound as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the jugular vein that flows out through the neck which is broken, and by the lack of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	leave the wound open with a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed for which we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound carefully, and stitch all around the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medicines that cause vomiting until they are clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that we should not do this unless the throat is completely stiffened, and the limbs are judged to be dead, and the defect is lost.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Therefore, cover the epiglottis because the hairs cannot be held, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	Therefore, the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to stitch the wound and heal, as long as it is healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young lady take a knife, and stab herself in her throat, and cut part of the throat veins.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I was called to cure her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not coughed blood or vomited, the blood flowed from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and cured it until she was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there was nothing left of the young lady but that she could speak, and she returned to her normal state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I know that in the region of the epiglottis there is no need to be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large swelling in the color of a grape, and it is very common in women.
et est selonc II manieres:	And it occurs in two ways:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental.
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	or natural, which has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidental one occurs in two ways, one of which is similar to a gouty swelling, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our blood vessel.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it does not require to be opened except in the small one that is in the neck, and it should be tested and searched in all the internal parts.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you have the knowledge to treat it as I do not, and cannot at all times, then the copper, as we copper the others, and take it out completely, if there is none.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And search well soon, and treat it as it should be, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	For the fire cautery
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of us are, which I will say all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And now it is necessary that I tell all the difference that is between us and others.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that others are cold and feverish, until the blisters are passed, and is accompanied by the purging;
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	Then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	Without the noise, there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains its own pus, which is according to the color of the blood, and begins like a small pimple, and becomes large;
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and are according to two appearances, either dry or moist, and many colors as I have said in the section.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to treat an unknown case, it is necessary to first examine and test the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses from us is that you grasp or more moist skin than you pierce in the abscess, and turn your fingers slowly and slowly, until you know that the instrument has perforated the center, then it is according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then, extract the mortise, and take care not to break it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If the moisture-filled wound is red, as it has been described in the other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if the mortise does not come out moisture afterwards, then scrape it to make it greasy, then cut it in a cross shape, and take out the splinters with pincers, and lightly scrape off all parts and keep the shirt where you took it from so that you can remove it clean with the new one.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot remove it clean, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If nothing stays in place, it returns to us many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it stays for a short time and does not cause harm, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, keep it clean, and use remedies to treat other injuries until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it is large, then cut out the two lips of the wound and treat what remains with charcoal.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if it is bleeding heavily and you cannot stop it, then apply the juice of broken glass to the wound and leave it for two or three hours until the bleeding stops, and rest the blood clot.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to the copper vessel that is left there.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See the shapes of the instruments used for opening veins, and they are in three ways:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small.
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and there are three parts that are called "lancet", and one that is called "bleeder", and there are three ways:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	large, medium, and small, to puncture the abscesses of the fistula;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like the needles that are used to make the spoons, and are of yellow gold, or of iron, or of silver, and cost as much as those that are already yellow, and are more easily broken than black ones for puncturing the sinuses of the fistula;
et sont de III manieres:	and there are three ways:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the amount of the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of needles are very similar, such as you see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if there are needles that have two barbs in three ways also.
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if there are needles that have three barbs, and are also in three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if there are needles that have two barbs, and needles of one barb only, and are also in three ways.
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	all of these are necessary in their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The heads of these are sharp, and of such there are some that cut only from one side, from which we skin the flesh, because we do not cut the vein or the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these intruders are the awls placed in palms, so that the pain does not persist at the opening of the abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	There are three ways:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	Great, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And we use only one from the limbs, such as legs, arms, breasts, and hips, and similar limbs.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never use any other small instrument, resembling the scraping of abscesses, in this form, to draw out blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is never put back in place that it should be aligned with veins, and arteries, and once again returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as long as they seem like breasts of a woman.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and prolong the inflated and swollen ones, and who want to heal them, if it is necessary according to this form of this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with healing ointment, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and heal it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and if the jaw is dislocated downwards, and is stuck due to its size, like in women, then make an incision into two ribs above, by making similar cuts.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	because one holds the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. to the line .g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then scrape the skin that is between the two jaws, and remove the fat, and follow what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	If it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the hairs do not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Let it remain until the remaining part and the fat are healed, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the heels
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the heels are ways of hard scabs or if they have cracks, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b to the line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole of the pus in the abscess is drained, apply old cotton to the wound and leave it on the other side, then remove all the cotton, and treat with a poultice suitable for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, then treat them as we have said about incising scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is cut, and the flesh above it is sound, then often there are abscesses, and just as often there is blood in the vein and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	And if one knows how to do it, then one should treat the abscess by making an incision along its length.
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel the pain, if you feel it tightly.
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then remove the apparent parts.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, and immediately when it is out of the ears and eyes and mouth and many other parts, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is therefore necessary to apply the iron cure, and the one at the top should also be applied, and in the one that is of inflating the artery by cutting from above the skin long.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then work the incision as small, and then separate the artery from the threads, until it is revealed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	Then, remove the arrow from one side, and pierce it through to the other side, and stretch the artery with a double thread of flax, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then, do not prick the limb that is between the two loops of an introducer until the pus that is inside comes out, and remove the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then, apply the remedy as I have instructed, until the wound heals.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then, treat the inflammation that comes from this, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	If the abscess is in the belly of the vein, it is necessary that you dip your hand in what you can of the abscess from all the skin, then draw out the needle outside the limb that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and if there is a double filament, so that you pull it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	Then tie the abscess as I have told you, or with one of two parts of the thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	And if you doubt that the thread will not hold, then put another needle all along the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four loops.
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut out the abscess until the excess is removed, then cut away the excess tissue and leave what is connected.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a soft cloth moistened with wine and oil on top, then treat with bandages and ointments until healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses come in the artery and the vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And there are often more remedies and instructions in all cases where there are joints, and this is the great abscess, and its color resembles the color of the flesh, and it is in many positions causing pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pressed, the pain is great, and it is not in front of the flesh, but outside the wound.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and moves well from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor out of place, and the one that is in joints does not need to be covered by iron:
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	by chance I may have contraction;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who are at the neck or face, make the skin to the sputum.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, then with needles, and the copper in its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suspend it at the tip, and scrape, then remove the bone, and stitch the wound to the seam, and the cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	of large swollen abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No times have occurred in the belly and no other place, and it is a disease that is called "funge" by the similarity of its appearance, and it is to the subtle roots, and the large joints;
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and there are small and very large ones;
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw the man who had two in his belly that were more like "funges" than any other thing, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had small roots, and were broken, and it flowed with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I took them and found in one eighteen ounces heavy, and in the other six ounces, and the workings in the incision are such that you look if the hairs are moist, and the color of the stone is white and moist and of subtle roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if the copper is wide at the tip, and they are in your presence with the fire cauterization.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For in cutting, there are often too large spurts of blood, and if you do not have it, then hurry to get the cauterizer.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the pain spreading and fearful of the incision with the knife, then take a well-made thread, and tie the wound as we have said, and leave it for two days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	and then tighten the bandage, and do not stop stretching the thread of cloth until it covers the wound, and cut through it with work.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	If the roots are large, then apply the cauterizing iron directly to the abdomen, but you should also cover half of it, then cauterize so it does not reappear.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cover the throul which is of a yellowish color and poor sensation and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these infected abscesses, I will come to treat them with leeches later.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the patient is feverish
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the boude comes from cauterizing a wound or cutting into a syphilitic ulcer, and it is above the abdomen and in some of the bruises, as it has in other wounds, or of blood that cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of moisture;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is by the rupture of the pus and by the outflow of the bile, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various sources.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is most diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides, it returns, and perhaps it is torn, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and by much work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is by moisture, it is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not force it much.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is by blood, it is open by these signs the abscesses are large and hard, and it is full of a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is by windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look whether its appearance is from the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary to leave the care.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if its appearance is for the intestine or the mucous, then you must command the patient to dye his linen, and be fully extended, then sign around the belly;
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have signed all over, then extend half of the abscess above all the large joint;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it around with a strong thread or a firm silk cord, and let the joint be loose;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then operate on half of the abscess extended over the joint, and let your knife indicate, and the intestine;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you have the truth of the joint, then dislocate it, and push the intestine to the side of the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you have the truth of the bone, then take it from the joint, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein opposes you, then go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads, and push the two needles around what you have done in order to pierce it.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then puncture the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the wound open until it can close, and cut off the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	when you cover it with a cloth when it is thin and raw, then treat it according to what is needed, and drain the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the arrow or the moisture that you have removed, then treat the limb according to what is needed, and soak the limb.
dou chancre	For the fire cauterization, instruct
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one must treat it with medicines, and how one must avoid the treatment of iron.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	and let us say the chancre is ingrown in the marsh, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancient ones said that when chancres are in a place where it can be removed as chancre which is in the mammary glands, and in the chest, and similar places, and everything should be removed when it is at the beginning.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, it does not matter that you approach it, for I have never been able to heal one.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	I have never seen anyone healed of one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And the workings, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purify once the evil of black bile;
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it heal if it has obvious accumulation, then remove the evil from the good limb to do the work;
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pour out your bile or pus, and the hair from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything.
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood clot completely, and clean the wound well with your hand or something else, and if the blood clots against the incision of the artery or vein, if it is not stopped by cauterization, it will cause harm.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then use other treatments until it is healed.
de ydropisie	de l’estomac
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have mentioned in the division, similar to hydrops, and how the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment given by medicines, and that which is cured by iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only illuminated;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	And one should not touch iron in these two similarities:
