c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	That is to say, tympanites and hypochondriac pain, for it is a deadly thing.
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	Therefore, when you treat this resemblance of dropsy which is called "eclises" of medicine, and the cure does not work, look if the pains are weak, or if he has another disease than dropsy, as most cases and similar things.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	If not, do not touch iron, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	And if you see the pain of great virtue, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is not too young or too old, then thus proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Hold the painful area straight above your hands, and the ministrants press the abdomen by bringing the sharp instrument to the lowest part of the belly, then take the spinous process according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be slicing of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	at a point, and ensure that no part is too thin so that it can come close to the intestine when inserted, and it cannot be broken;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then look if the hernia is pushed towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary that you cut them off at the base of the three fingers directly above the wrist;
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the hernia is due to the disease of the liver, then your incision should be on the left side of the base of the three fingers;
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	If it is due to the muscle, then it should be set to the right, and it should not be moved only by the hairs growing over the wound where the excess does not run to the weak limb.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and beat it, and lift your hand to the entire space between the skin and the flesh as if you are scraping in the quantity of an egg or around.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	Then pierce the flesh until the space between the skin and the flesh reaches the desired length, and this is the width of the needle, then remove it, and beat this instrument with which this form is made:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	And it is similar to a thin silver chain, and is made of light iron or copper, and has a small hole in its center.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three holes;
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on the other;
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is cut like a feather, and its shape is like the incision that the scribe makes when carving the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of it is the quill, so that when the instrument comes to the tip, then place the instrument above the quill;
vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	empty the half or third part, for if you empty it more than it should be at that hour, by chance it may cause the patient to die from the resolution of his spirit from the arm, or he loses consciousness, or he approaches death;
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz;	but according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue mean, and its hairs.
puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere;	then take the tool and hold the sharp edge, and it is held now for the one who is supposed to pierce the part that is above the eyelid, of which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner;
puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	then restart the tool the other day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take a small amount of the sharp edge;
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	do this every day, and guard against following too much until it does not delay but only a little sharp edge.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre;	And if you doubt the pain, and you leave it too long without proper care, then the wound of burial or sand heals, and by much sweat or bathing and in the sun, and it becomes infected with drinking;
et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	and the treatment of desiccative medicines until it is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the arrow, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the removal of the probe
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born without a wart in the penis, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to pierce at all times with a very thin needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet;	then put or puncture a thin needle through the bottom, and tie it and leave it for three days or four and when he wants to make urine, if it is removed, and make urine, and then put it back;
et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	And by chance, it does not cover well, because the urine that comes out does not keep it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is pricked is small, it is treated with a thin thread of the bottom, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut;	Those who do not have the perineum in their joint are disabled, because no one is born with the perineum at the top of the thigh, so they cannot urinate before their thigh rises.
et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	And they cannot urinate because the matter cannot come out through the urethra, and it is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient;	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs grow on top of their back, and the thigh bone and the hip are like the belly of a pen, so that the perineum is in the middle, as it should be.
et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and guard against the evacuation of blood which often occurs, and if it does, if the cloth that stops the bleeding is used, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide;	often come these worms in the tail, and it is an ugly appearance of a maggot;
et en i a malignes et non malignes;	and there are both harmful and not harmful ones;
si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien;	if it is necessary that you remove them with fine tweezers, and pick up and clean all of them, then put on a piece of Egyptian gauze;
puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of the wound continues until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the wound is malignant, with a putrid color and foul smell, then you must cauterize it with fire.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier;	When you have coped with it, and if the dislocation is in the socket and part of it is inside the skin and part outside, then you must first break the dislocation that is inside.
et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	and when it is broken, if the part outside is healed.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion;	For when you heal it together, if the part of the bone is not secure, and there is blackness and corruption in its socket and where it was connected.
si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then you must remove all that is black and corrupted, then apply the plaster of honey and flour made from the shells of large pumpkins and vetch, then heal with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood flows, then treat the lunar cauterization according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble:	The cautery helps with two positions together:
c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption;	namely, at the extraction of arrows, and in decay;
et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi;	and if the patient is corrupt and retreats, it is necessary that you beat or conduct the stick a cane of mud, and urinate on the painful parts;
et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	and when the skin has erupted at the head of the stick which have been those who were not circumcised, or it has for wound or abscess, then it is necessary that you scorch it with the instrument of the beard, until the pus is removed, and deliver the patient from all parts of the stick;
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil;	and if it is a bad thing to divide the vein, then you must burn it at the spot with no part of the spoon and the hair;
puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	then dry thoroughly between two, and put on a thin layer of linen cloth wet with cold water, that it does not blister.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies;	Circumcision is not different from other wounds in continuity;
toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	all the same when we do this work of our intent, and properly in children, it is a matter that we should do the best work, and the lightest to save.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule;	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and wise men who did circumcision in the middle, and with force, and all at once;
si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	if there were two curtains, because there is two, and by chance if one covers the other above and delays the other below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre;	or it recovers covered, and the pain is double, and to the wound that is from the tip of the member is not sure.
et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	and to the wound of the finger by chance the iron escapes and ruins the work, and many times they are born so that they do not have a need for wound treatment and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound healing that is done with force to all the member of the thread, I found the best of the experiment, for the forces cut equally as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens;	For when you press your hand, if you cut evenly in all the soft parts;
mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir;	but that the thread is well stretched around the skin;
et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	And the way of the first work is that you make the child think that you are only tying the thread around the stick as much as possible, and then throw it in all ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens;	Then place the child straight between your hands, and hide the forces between your hands or away from your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments.
puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens;	Then blow your hand on the stick and gently, and pull it up as high as the child's stick is long.
puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien;	Then wipe it well of the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it away from one side to the other.
et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	and the second line is to be done by the second hand with the pouch and the correct index, and between the two lines, then lift the head carefully and take the tip of the staff;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres;	then let the blood flow slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous;
et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and put powder on and on the powder a glue made from the unsalted fat of a well-cooked hare, tempered with rose vinegar, boiled in rose oil and fresh, and let it stay overnight, and the other cure until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste:	The form of forces for the mummification is this:
li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The two shoulders are tense and thin, and the shoulders are also as great as the hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision;	The error of the mundification is that the knife is not cutting into the incision;
donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme;	Therefore, you must extend it to your angle, as well as when the legs make an abscess;
et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	and the coping equally, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then hold it with nails, and then the coping.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement;	And if they pass three hours, and what is outside the rod is swollen, then let it remain until the abscess is completely healed, and scrape lightly;
si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If you move the cup as you can, and avoid the part of the staff, it will not harm you.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point;	Therefore, cure the limb of things that cause pain from powder, as we have said or treated for powders, and if you use too much care, it will not harm.
cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, cure the limb as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	The retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or frozen blood, or a bowel, or a charred, or similar things, as we have said in the division.
et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz;	and if the urine is not released, and you see that retention is due to a stone that is lodged in the urethra, then it is necessary that the painful parts be lifted over the knees.
et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet;	and the feet should be placed on the back, and extend the belly from the upper part of the back, and restrain the painful parts as much as possible.
et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	and then the belly is pressed against the expression of the stone from above, so that the urine is released and;
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme:	and if it does not come, as we have said, and the painful parts are greatly painful, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe", of which this is the form:
et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil;	and let it be of fine silver wire, as like a quill of an eagle.
et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	and let the needle be of a long and half-palm, and fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue;	And the manner of the issue of the urine is that you take a double thread, and tie the head to the tip of the cotton or wool, and pull the head of the thread through the tube.
et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	and fold the excess of the wool and pull it to the head of the tube, then oil the tube with oil or butter and egg white, and place the patient on a chair, and the arose the bladder and the oil-soaked cloth and oil of olive and vinegar.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude;	Then lightly insert the syringe into the bone, until it reaches the root of the bone, then double the bone over against the wound.
puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors;	Then push the syringe forward towards the bladder, and feel the hairs coming out of the empty space, and this is only done in this order if the guide or it goes is twisted.
puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then stretch the thread along the entire thread slowly and slowly, and the urine follows the thread, then remove it forcefully, and correct the urine.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And restart the syringe until the bladder is empty and the hairs are aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or blood come into the bladder, and putrefaction is assembled, and you see distillation of water and medicines, then use all the tool called «clepsedre», and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus:	It is closed, and if it has three holes:
II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois;	On one side, and on the other, as you see;
et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	And the joint is cut by the doctor's knife in such a way that it does not damage the bone too much, so that the moisture can be drawn out and put back as necessary.
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens;	And when you see your medicines going into the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and draw it out through the opening that is there.
si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens;	If you draw out the moisture with the catheter, then push the catheter strongly back in.
si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	If the moisture enters again, and comes to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie:	And this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheterizes the bladder:
si est ci:	If it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut;	And it is of silver or of copper, and it is the highest of the catheters;
et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet;	And it is thinner at the top where the catheter enters;
puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu;	Then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you saw catheterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts with a double thread of wool, and heat the moisture above the fire;
puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	Then put the tip of the catheter in the hole, then hold your hand over the bladder all around the moisture, until the pain feels that the moisture has reached the bladder;
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor;	and if you do not have a catheter, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle with it, and pierce it roundly around;
puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument;	then stuff the thread strongly into these holes, then assemble the circle as one would assemble a shield, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it with the instrument;
et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	and do as you have done with the catheter, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the catheter.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines;	We have said in the previous section the ways of arrows and extraction together with medicines;
et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille;	and I have said the difference between the arrow embedded in the flesh and all the signs, and in what arrow one should make an incision;
et en la vessie, et en la verge;	and in the bladder, and in the penis;
et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	and I will tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit;	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the sharp urine spray from the bladder is like a sharp blow to its subtlety.
et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist;	and there is a sharp pain in the penis, and it often hurts, and then it becomes inflamed.
et a mout de ces saut li fondemens;	and with many of these sprays, the base.
et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece;	and is light in the healing of children up to the age of four, and is very painful in old men, and is constantly present, among those who are between young and old.
et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	And the treatment of those with large stones is lighter than that of those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with cloth, to draw out all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never clogs when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut;	Then take the dislocation by the feet, and stand and move it towards the outside, so that the stone descends to the edge of the bladder, and never once rise up from the hip.
puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval;	Then let it sit between your hands and prepare it, with its hands away from its thighs, so that the bladder is completely descending down.
puis la quier et la touche dedens;	Then grasp and touch inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis;	And if she does not break at the touch of the soft touch, then gently press your index finger of your right hand, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull;
et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie;	and press at its base, and cut into the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, if the pain is in the groin, then apply the anointing oil to the affected area;
puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	then press above your finger, and cut at the place where you saw it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille;	And command the minister to press the anus with his hand, and command him to stretch the testicles to his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is outside the testicles in the part where the incision is made;
puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	Then apply the splint, covering it with a cloth:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre;	And make an incision between the thighs and the groin, not in the middle but on the right side of the naval:
et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And the incision should be straight above the stone, and the two ends should be at the thigh or groin, and the width of the cut should be wide on the outside and narrow in the middle, according to the size of the stone, not too wide:
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail;	If the pressure is too great where it is at the groin, it may jump out of place:
et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges:	And check if there are any stones or edges and margins:
si est griés a issir;	if it is grasped to pull out;
et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	and if there is a smooth, rounded part, like a bone, and its exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant;	In such cases where it has angles and edges, make the cut larger;
et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe;	and if it does not jump out, then you must force it with pincers that are like a lime at the head to pull the stone so it does not escape;
ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief;	or you can push it out with a subtle hooked instrument from the head.
et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	and if you cannot engage it thus, then enlarge the small hole, and if there is no skin, then strain it with vinegar.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are more than one arrow, first remove the largest one from the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then pull it out, and the smaller ones afterward if there are many.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is very large, then it should be cut, and a larger wound made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide:	For two things happen to the dislocated joint:
ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder;	or it dies, or the urine comes out through the wound because the joint cannot hold together.
mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	but all effort must be made to pull it out or remove it with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut;	And when you have completed your work, apply incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, bind it, and place a moist cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and vinegar and cold rosewater, to alleviate the inflammation.
puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Then resolve the misalignment over its shoulder, and do not dislocate the joint further by pulling it too hard.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, the limb should rise well with oil and vinegar, then apply a healing ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine:	And if pus comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and it is retained by the urine, which is known to be withheld without causing a sensation when urinating.
boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	Therefore, remove the pus from the wound, and extract that blood clot, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause damage.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then lift the wound of the sharp and the silk and the silk thread, and assist in all ways that you can, until it is healed.
et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And it is necessary that all the wounds that you treat, that you tie the two thighs together, and gather the remedies above the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir;	And if the stone is small, and it is guided by a catheter, and tied up, and the urine cannot come out;
si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	if the cure that I have said before, that you cut many times, is excused from this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this before.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three angles tied with a thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie;	Then take a thread and tie it around the catheter outside the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder;
puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere;	then gently push the thread into the catheter until it reaches the stone;
et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part;	and then turn the chisel to your hand on the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side.
si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	if soon comes the urine, then press your hand above the part that remains of the stone that is inside the shaft.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	If it is already broken, and it springs forth with the urine, and is sharp against the hairs;
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie;	and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread below the stone and the other above, then make the shaft in the place between the two threads, then pull it out, and remove the thread, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the care as long as they are healthy.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses:	Few have seen a needle inserted into women, and if it ever happens, then the care is difficult, and it is prohibited for three reasons:
l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge;	the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin;
et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-trained who would willingly expose herself to such shame, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains;	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well-trained in this art of hands;
et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil;	and the fourth reason is that if the woman's needle is larger than the man's, because it should be made with a deeper cut, and there is great fear. And if necessary, one must send for a skilled midwife, and apply the truthful herb, and if you do not know how to do this, then it is not advisable to try to perform the procedure yourself;
et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	and if a woman presents with a sharp pain in her life, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and she commands that she do what you command of the examination of the stone;
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge:	and look very closely if the woman is virgin:
adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere;	then it is necessary to put her hand or base and search for the stone;
et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	and if she finds it, then hold her hand away from her base, and recommend that she put her hand or with the pain, and press her right hand firmly on the anus.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse;	if she finds it, then it is necessary to move it from great to great from the entrance of the anus until it reaches the root of the thigh;
puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;	Then cut across the stone in the root of the thigh, against the middle of the knee, where it is muscle-filled and feels like a stone in that part.
et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	And do not move the joint above or below the stone, and let the wound heal at first small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont:	Then push the stone out of the wound, if you feel the stone so sharp that the stone can be removed, and note that many methods of stones are:
c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	It is to know, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and those that have edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	And if it does not come out, then put the broken glass in the wound, and let it stay there an hour until the stone is softened.
puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	then return to your work, until the stone is fully removed, and have the instruments I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for you to help in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide;	and if it bleeds again, and it is from the artery that has been cut, then put powder on the wound and bandage it with tents and binders, and do not restart, and leave the stone and do not pull it out, unless by chance it might kill the patient.
puis cure la plaie.	then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound healed, then return to your work, until the stone is formed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef;	Ramming with water is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white clay, which is not the same as the juice of herbs that contain the urine.
et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;	and is called "syfac", and never properly in the web of the eyelid, if one cares that it is not the other eyelid.
et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit;	and it is the thin skin between the white "syfac" that we have said.
et ceu n’avient se poc non.	and it does not have a specific name.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this branch is due to weakness that comes from within, and it is spread out that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors:	And never if it comes from percussion on the eyelids, and this moisture has many colors:
ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	or it is a changing color from yellow to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and there are more.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is the white "syfac" that we have said, then the abscesses are there, and they are long like the shape of an eyelid, and do not open the eyelids, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	If he has moisture in his own cloth, then the abscesses are treated with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought to be another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien;	and if his moisture is between the skin of the fingers and the white nail, he feels it well.
donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the introducing parts, because it was previously formed.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes afterwards, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors;	And when we cure them with iron, it is necessary that the hairs be cleaned according to some power and the replenishment of his body.
puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	then the swine on his back, on something a little high, and put much cloth over him.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions;	then lift up his right arm, and command the assistant to lift it on the left side, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the armpit.
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	then take the spatula and cover the skin of the ribs with the long part up to the knuckle, and make your cut straight across the skin of the ribs towards the white face, and gently scrape the skin according to the power.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont;	then pierce the white face flat with a wide needle, and extract all the sharp points, then put your needles, and press the white face upwards.
et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement;	and do not touch the face of the bones, but only the skin.
cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	remove all or even the very ribs of him, if you do not remove them properly, then it will return to sharp.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac;	and if the bone jumps up at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the skin.
puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then sew the two books of the face of the bones to a seam, then treat it as the other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc;	and if you break the bone and it becomes infected with another disease, then it is necessary to tie the veins that are suspended, in doubt of blood clotting.
puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	Then copper the coin to all the suspensory, and extract the eye, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices;	And if it is sharp and gathered in two parts together, they are two branches;
si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	If you copper the other part evenly as you did the first, then wipe the blood, and put some soft cloth soaked in rose oil into the wound;
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and put some other soft cloth soaked in wine and oil under the two copper pieces, and put on top doubled cloths, and tie it to all the limb that is according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil;	Then take two cloths, and place them like this charpie according to this appearance, and they are sewn together at the girdle of the breeches, and one of the strings above the buttocks, and the other at the part of the elbow;
et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	and the other two heads above the two angles, and let all the assembly be restrained in the loop of the brace.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	and never use this branch of the cautery in the shape of an iron needle, and you must grip the cauterizing needle subtly, and coat the skin with it, and heat it as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the acid is discovered;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	if you take the cauterizing needle in this form, and pierce that white sap with one prick, and burn the skin with this subtle cauterizing;
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout;	and coat it in all ways that you can, until you extract everything;
et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef;	and beware that the fire does not touch the eyeball.
et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve;	and cleanse this work is safer.
et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	and avoid the corruption of blood, and keep quiet the works of tailoring.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	and if nothing goes against you, or abscess in the groin or corruption of blood or other thing, then cure what goes against you according to what is said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit;	And if the pain is not severe, and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then alleviate perforation, as I told you, and it is that when you are well certain by the signs that we have said that the aqueous humor is low, then place the pain on the raised seat;
pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors;	For the abscess, pierce it in the outermost part, and place the incision along the length of the body;
et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	and make the incisions wide enough that all the sharp pain is relieved;
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then place cotton on the limb, and tie it, and let the remaining sharp pain subside, then treat the wound until it is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant;	and if the white cloth does not prevent the sharp pain from escaping through the wound mouth, then you must use a pen or the instrument used to treat hydrophobia, of which the form is as previously mentioned;
et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and enlarge the wound slightly, and remove that which is sharp so that it returns to its agility after six months or more, and when it is assembled as before, and thus passes through its pains.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	There are many fearful conditions in the cutting of this branch, which seems to me that it is better to leave;
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	and I will tell you the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions;	I say therefore that many abscesses come from wounds, and immediately after cutting;
et c’est par mout de cas.	and it is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is to know by excessive sharp and wet, which is spread after cutting, or from impact;
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors;	and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the blood flow;
et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	and it does not cause pain, and it is a serious abscess;
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	and sometimes it is a gray, pussy, and purulent abscess, of yellowish color, and never comes from an artery or a vein swelling;
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is from an artery, it is known by the appearance of the abscess, which changes when you press on it with your fingers;
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and it does not require that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	Those that come from vein swelling are known by their appearance at the touch of your fingers, and can often be cut across this resemblance, and on the others as well;
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and you must cut the cords that are causing the swelling, then set the bone in place, and the wound is cleaned with a white cloth, and deliver the suspended parts from all parts of the bone.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the bone is already set with these charms, then you must cut the bone and the cords.
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	and if it is outside the skin or inside the veins, then you must deliver all of that which is held, and clean it thoroughly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the horn of the char is located behind the shoulder, it is necessary that you cut it all, and extract the eye, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with a linen cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then use other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping similar to a boil, with the softening of the cords, and the pain increases when it moves.
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	And the treatment of this disease is as difficult and painful as the one before, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	It is necessary that you make the patient sit upright on an elevated seat, then lift the suspensor of the testicles to your fingers, and all the veins that are close to the cord, and clean them with a master's hair, and stretch them properly.
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	Then cut across the sharp spatula through the middle of the veins, until they are exposed, and then scrape each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then fish out an needle or he has a double thread, and tie it to the first shoulder where the blood came from, and to the other shoulder.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut across the middle straight, according to the length of the wound, and remove the corrupted blood.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as with others, using bandages or ointments, so that no one knows what the wound was.
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for because of this there is no harm, and if all the people see it, then you must remove the bandages from everyone.
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	if he does not lose his appearance because of the incision of the bandages, and they dry and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The symptoms of this branch are due to the section that comes out or sphincter, or extension over the abdomen in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from that break to one of the bones;
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes:	and this break is due to too much sphincter, or from extension of it, and these two ways come from many causes:
ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	or from impact, or from jumping, or from shouting, or from lifting heavy weights, and similar things;
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is due to too much sphincter, are that it happens slowly and gradually, over a long time, and does not come suddenly;
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscesses are equal up to the backbone, because the face is close to the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the tooth, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and has various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and it is for the end of the intestine and the heart behind the tooth.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the worms are found with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the illness, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron with fear, because it should be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of the work is that you command or let the patient bend the intestines with their hand into the wound, if it can be pushed in.
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then it should be even above his neck, between your hands, and loosen the bowels.
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then the wound should be above, and cover all the skin of the bones.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then push in between the belly's lips an incision according to what you have skill for opening the wound, and let them be such that the intestines can issue.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then shave the beard that is under the skin of the flesh, until the white beard is exposed from all parts.
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac;	then insert your index finger in the roof of the mouth that leads to the flesh, between the white beard that is under the skin of the cheek, and between the second beard, and behind the cheek, and between the second beard.
et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and then move the cheek outwards from the skin of the flesh, and place the white beard on top of your right hand, and lift the cheek towards the back, and pull all the beard downwards towards the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and commands the minister to stretch the arm upward, and release the air that is behind the ligament;
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and asks if he has any intestines wrapped or white and hard, and if you find anything, then let it go out of the stomach;
puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions;	then take a needle or he has thick thread made of many threads, and insert it into the back part of the white and hard thing, which is after the skin of the intestines;
aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz;	then after the belly, then cover the threads that appear from the threads, until there are four threads;
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars;	then assemble them one above the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the white and hard thing, which we have said is out of the skin of the intestines, with a strong thread of two parts;
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	Then envelop the dislocated shoulder in two parts, so that no part of the clothing that they wear can enter into the wound, as an abscess does not come.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	And immediately apply the bandage according to the first bandage, with two fingers of that, and after these two bandages leave the sucking wound which is outside the curvature of the bones, the great one of a finger.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte;	And then the other according to the round shape that the evil carries;
puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	Then cover in the part that is outside the skin of the bones, as much as possible without correction, and the bone, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply a poultice of soft cloth in oil to wounds, and it applies the remedy that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have said, after incision, due to fear of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui;	For this has often happened, and let the remedy remain until it heals through it;
et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	and if it takes too long to settle, then apply hot vinegar, and place on what we have said, until it heals.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	then treat the wound with other remedies, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made in such a way as the branch that is together with the face, in some manner that you bind the veins, after the cut above the belly lightly at the opening;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient;	then copulate with me, and heal the abscess of this which works, until the vessels are clean.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the cure as we have said, until they are healthy.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus;	No time comes when there is a break or tear, as we have said, and open the veins;
et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	and do not cut any of the intestines as we have said, and if there are any, it is little, and repair them every hour;
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	and whenever if he remains too long in this point, the wound or the abscess, until the intestines are cut;

et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit;	and if it is by cauterization, as we have previously mentioned.
et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	and never cured in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois;	and the hairs are often tied together above their backs between your hands, then the limb of the tear is filled with a large amount of three fingers worth.
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	then the sinew that is outside the skin that surrounds it, then take the needle and put it on the limb appearing from the sinew;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press it against the front of the belly, then cut the two limbs appearing from the sinew above the head of the needle, and cut both.

puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Then treat it with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you remove the arrows, if you do not defile and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The saphenous vein is constrained, and does not appear in the incision, and the cauteries are silent in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir;	Many times have the tendons of the joints been softened in some men, because the charms that are inside are softened, and it is to be seen.
et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil;	And it is a matter, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the pain lie on its back, and the copper which is softened over the natural skin;
puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement;	Then gather the two lips to one seam, and if you see, cut first the excess of the softened skin at three or four seams firmly.
puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Then, apply between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds, until it is healed, and cut off the thread.
dou chastrement	forcibly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre;	It is customary in our law to use cauterization, and because I would like not to speak of it in this book;
et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres:	and it is not necessary for any other way:
dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure;	one of which is that the patient responds to the cauterization when asked about it, and in this way treat it.
et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	and the other, because we often have to cauterize animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and chickens and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres:	I therefore say that this chapter is done in two ways:
ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	or by traction, or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant;	In the one that we make by traction, we should sit the patient best in high heat, until the ligaments are softened and during.
puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	then hold them with your hand, until they are put back and you do not feel them anymore.
Du chastrement de taille:	Of the sacrament of the belly:
covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez;	You should clean the patient, and press the skin of the ligaments with your right hand, then tie the suspenders, and cover each burn separately, when you have them well scorched.

et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure;	and this method of castration is more dangerous than that which is done by attraction, because at attraction something from the testicles remains, by which the animal desires sexual intercourse;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes:	Hermofrodite is according to two ways:
l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	the first is that between the two testicles open as much as the figure of a woman's nature, or he has hair, and sometimes cutting it allows urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has above the clitoris as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies;	And the treatment of males and females is that you cut off all the hairs stuck together, and treat them as other wounds;
en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	In the second manner, for men whose urine springs from their clothing, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir;	Tentingene is a charm placed on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see.
et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	And no women have it as big as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement;	It is necessary for you to stain the excess of the tentingene on your hand or nails, and wipe it off lightly.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And do not go too far back, for there is no blood coming, then the cure of other cures until it is clean.
et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	and in another chariot that is born from the mouth of the marsh, and it uses, and perhaps it jumps up, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and because of this they call it the ancient "cowdisease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary for you to grasp it, as we have said about the protrusion, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	If it is necessary for you to grasp it
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis;	It is indeed difficult to determine the nature of a woman's pregnancy, or when it is small.

ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit;	Or it is by charm, or a subtle or spelled spell, and it is made to happen in the marsh, or in the cost, or outside, or wherever it may be.

des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul;	Emorroides are openings of veins without a cut as usual, and when the emorroides are old they become thrombi.
et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	And we have said in the previous section the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.

Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	If one hand comes before the other and it cannot be brought back by constriction, then you must wrap it around a pole, until it is completely healed.
puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	Then the copper wire should be placed in the joint of the foot or at the heel, and thus you must do in the other hand, and to the two feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue;	And if the child's head is large and it is difficult to deliver, or if it has an acute angle assembled, then you must push the spatula with sharp edges between your fingers, and make the head and extract the acute angle.
ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	or you must break it with the instrument called "almidach", of which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that is after this one.
et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment;	And thus, even if he himself is of great natural stature.
et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer;	Then pull the bones apart with pincers, and if he jumps and is held by the forceps, then they are cut as much as possible until the moisture that is out comes out.
et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues;	And if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces with a knife that you can.
et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if it is inflated in the belly or out of the ribs, then you must pierce it until the moisture runs out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	If the infant is held above its feet, then the traction is light, and the pressure on the marsh is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main;	And if it is swollen in the belly or in the groin, then you must extract it by pulling it out through the wrapped cloth with your hand.
et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre;	And making the belly or the ankle, until the moisture that is in it is corrected.
et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	And if the other member is broken and the patient cannot move it, then bring a cup of water to his mouth and let him drink.
puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer;	Then drink one or two, and remove it.
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	And if the patient's mouth is retracted due to an abscess that has come, then it is not necessary to force, but it is necessary to administer moist and fat things.
