Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	If the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Take the bone, and strain it at the top of the bone that opens, and command it to extend upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and put another thinner thread of linen below the first thread, and tie it above the wound that is on the bone, and extend the head, so that you can remove the rotten flesh from outside, and uncover the wound above the limb where you want it to be, so that it does not become infected.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a bandage or a cloth outside the bone to cover the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it should be as visible and feelable as possible to see and feel the corruption, and should be another time.

et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or the nerve not cause you harm.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and scrape away what the incisor and the threads for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and the appearance of teeth, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.

si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you understand the tool that you have according to what it should be used.
dou feu	with great fire

et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs are such that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and then it turns darker, as in the corrosion of one member by another, and it takes hold of the whole body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if you have a copper vessel, and if it is by the impact of some poisonous animals, such as scorpions and vipers and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the penis, and the copper, and do not give him any space for the venom to come to his hand.

et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And as soon as the corrosion comes or pain:

et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the manner of binding or covering the limb is such that you tie it above and below, and extend some bandages along one side, and other bandages along the other side, and you wet the skin between the two sides to the width of a span, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then cover or bind with cloth, and put a piece of linen on each part, so that the cloth does not touch the healthy limb, and avoids other injury and abscess;

et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to the man in that case:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	a dark spot appeared that seemed like a burn from fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his toe, which spread to the entire foot;

regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look to see if the breasts are large, and the nipple is of foul smell, then plaster with Egyptian medicine made as follows:

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	Panarice is an abscess that arises outside the joint of the little finger of the hand, or of the foot, or by chance arises in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	And when it is removed, and no attention is paid, if it comes back with an abscess, and corrode and pour boiling water as much as it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it corrodes all of it;

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sore hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The pain that arises in the hands of some men by chance is all charred, and by chance it has a tail or where it has bones, and once it has an angle, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or where the birth is in any of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those born without any bone do not move, and those born at the joint of the bone may move.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of one who is chubby is lighter, in a way:

Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	Those born at the root of the joint are difficult to cure.
si te tien dou coper.	if you hold it with a cover.

In those who are born or should be at the back, it is necessary that you first cut the rounded part of the bone to the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable silk for this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The same things that come together in two ways, either by birth or by wounding, or by burning of fire, or by similar things.

puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	Then put between two bandages or cloths, moistened with rose oil, so that they do not stick.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	between two thin pieces of cloth, as much as the joint should be heard, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of them comes with their palm, then apply it as it should be.
des vils	of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Vis are veins large and swollen filled with superfluous melancholic fluids, which come from many members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more often in the legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Then you must administer them purgative of clyster, and then the healthy one from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment of iron is according to two methods:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is that it is removed and the black blood is drawn out.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other method is that the vein is opened and all the blood is drawn out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The abdomen is thus according to this manner:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	The first leg is raised high and hot, so that the big toe is not thinned, then strain the leg with the bad side down towards the lower part of the belly;
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then open the vein in the belly, in I, II or III, of a wide-bore needle, then release and pull out the black blood to your hand, from one to the other, until as much blood as the bad side can bear is drawn;
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	then bind it and command that he be fed with foods seasoned with black pepper;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	And begin the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are flat, and exposed to the air.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The following is the method for this:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Rub the affected leg with oil, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and apply hot water to the leg until it becomes red, and swell the veins;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, heat the water at the fire, and then apply it to the vein where it is long, at the base of the knee, or in the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then scrape the skin at the base of the vein, and remove all parts of it until it appears when touched;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and it appears red and black, and when it enters or skin seems to resemble a white cord.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then press the raw flesh out of the skin, until it is raised from the skin, and then it can be removed with a light touch, then the copper in the other joint for about three days.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it to the wound, as you have done, and remove it with a light touch, as you did before.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then remove another size, or if you have skill, then lift it and remove it to the other side of the wound, then cut and remove it from the second size.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it from the abdomen, as much as it can be removed, then cover it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, then insert a large needle into the intestine strongly doubled, and tie it and pull it out, and turn your hand from one side to the other, as much as there is.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and be careful that it does not cover, because if it covers, then it cannot be pulled or lifted, and it causes harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and when you have treated it all, then place on the wound of the sore linen soaked in wine and in red oil;
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and the cure as long as he is healthy.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if his sight is contracted and twisted and clouded together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must forcefully untwist it, but do not cover it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of iron that covers the eye if is curved, and does not cut through, so it does not cover the vein;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of large curvature, because if it were thin, it would cover the vein, but if it is large as we have said, and this is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the vein of the eye
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is incised in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in land where there is no moisture;
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and by chance it arises in another part than the legs, and this has the pus that comes out of the skin, as it comes from inside the flesh and muscles, incise between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the limb changes, and the wound begins to protrude, like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the wound is open, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plaster of one and a half to two fingers thick, and the plaster, and leave the plaster on the leg, and every time it is not there, if you wrap it around the plaster, and the plaster.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	And if it is too long, cut off a part, wrap it around, and not cover the remaining part at its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	For if you cut it off, it will enter into the wound and cause abscess and putrefaction or sickness in the limb, and it will be very bad.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For this reason, it is necessary to treat it little by little just at the head, and nothing should remain or rot.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	And there is never this vein when it is treated from the palm of length, or of X, and some have come to me, from which it issues of X lengths, and when you cut it off, it will burst or puncture, and it will perforate just at the bottom, so that everything will be out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and clear out the matter that is inside, and administer to the patient medicines in the form of poultices every day, then treat the wounds as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never rain on this vein, and especially when it opens at the joint of the finger, or the finger, and much pressure comes out, and it suddenly rains;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	treat the wound as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called in our land "bull disease", because it often affects bulls, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body up and down, and is felt well at the alert of member to member, as long as it does not leave the skin where it was;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by the corruption of some humors, such as worms coming from and wriggling in the intestines and lumbrics and ascarides or worms in the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and its harm is doubted, for when it goes through the body, and climbs to the head, and comes to the oil, by chance it enters, and destroys the oil.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	This happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cure and draw, one cannot help but notice when it goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	Therefore, it is necessary to tie the limb above and below a very tight bandage, then cut it off and draw it out, and if it turns black in the char, you should not touch it, but cauterize it with fire until it dies.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is that it corrupts the oil, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming or close to the oil, hold it firmly away from it, then cover it and remove it.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is advisable to use the remedy of applying a solution of medicinal herbs for the bad humors that cause disease, and if it fails to work, try using meat broths for purgation.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain coming from the windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called in our land "wakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member;
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I will tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered that one of her arms was swollen, and there was a small boil in the vein of the arm.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	And soon after, it grew as big as a worm in the shoulder, much faster than anything, just like quick silver when it is cut from lead.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	The pain separated from the arm and moved to the shoulder, and then a little later it rotted throughout the body, until it reached the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then she told me that she turned around inside the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how she moved from one limb to another, for I had never seen this disease in this way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted to move the pain from one arm to the other, but I could not do so, as I saw in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, and her veins were exposed, and because that whiteness appeared constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not reveal themselves to those who are delicate, and who have moist skin and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see how to cure this disease, and the pain feels as we have said, if it opens up as we have described, then tie above and below quickly, and then cover it with a bandage until that whiteness is released from the limb.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the limb.
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it in your eyes, then treat the cause of that whiteness, as with foul-smelling pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, according to their resemblances and according to the materials they are made of.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their shapes is such that there are those with large points, small points, curved points, and smoothed points.
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those who have II angles, and of those who have tongues, and of those which have pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	And that which pierces into any member however it pierces in the manner:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or in the principal member which is hairy, such as the head, neck, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it pierces therefore into any part of these members, and the sign of death, which I will tell you afterwards, is apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	if it is necessary to extract this arrow, for many die afterwards in various positions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not completely embedded, then remove it, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of the skull when the arrow pierces and penetrates the bone, and the syphilitic pus that is above the skull, is when there is scotomy and soda and swelling and confusion, and inflammation and swelling of the tongue, and spasms and mental confusion, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps there is no force in the nostrils, or in the ears.
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps the tongue and voice are affected;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and white pus-like matter issues from the wound, and also like bruised meat;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	if this sign appears to you, then take care of the patient, and remove the arrow if it is not already out.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it pierces or breaks, is that it is near the right breast, and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the arrow moves as if it were stuck in something, and also cuts through black blood, and causes coldness and cold sweat, and syncope:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, with doubt, they send them away.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign that the arrow has not been pulled out is that without any pain, bubbles come out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the limb changes color, and the patient breathes high and seeks for the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrowhead pierces through the covering of the worst, it is under the small ribs;
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and causes great pain and breathlessness.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and they move all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrowhead pierces the stomach, by chance if something undigested from the meat does not come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrowhead pierces the abdomen, and nothing comes out through the intestines, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrowhead pierces through the bladder, and the urine spurts out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain:
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	Therefore, that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and back and spine and hip and knee and leg, and similar members, are safe according to many positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because of what you were doing differently.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who was shot in the calf at the root of the knee:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it, and pulled it out from the other side of the fat of the ear, and was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And if a splinter enters the skin and gets stuck in the oil paper outside the paper, and the splinter is replaced, and it cannot be reached except with the tip towards the top, and it was a large splinter like a Turkish arrow, through all the iron without ears;
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	the wound was cleansed, and no bad accidents came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And if a splinter enters the throat of a Christian, and the splinter is Arabic-shaped with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I removed the barbs, and carefully extracted it until I got it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I drew a spear from a man, which was stuck in his neck or stomach, and thought he was dying.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	Then after thirty days, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the spear above, and pulled it out, and removed it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you want to a man who has a spear sticking out of his back, and the wound was sewn up above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and the spear remained inside him, and did not change his natural condition, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And you see another man, who has a spear sticking out of his face, and the wound was sewn up;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and prolongs thus without suffering great pain;
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And a arrow was removed from the man of the king, who had it sticking out of his throat, and was slightly tilted to the right side;
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and the arrow was completely embedded.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called for after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If the wound is very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I found it all under a thin tent, and did not feel anything;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt sharp pain and pain on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put some warm and soothing ointment on his forehead because the veins were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the bones of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I put the plaster on immediately, and poured it directly onto the wound, and it remained there for a long time, until he felt the arrow inside his nostril.
et il le me dist.	and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I put the corrosive medicine on the wound immediately, and I tried it, and I felt the tip of the arrow that was lodged in the bone.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I pushed it into the opening of the wound with that medicine, until the arrow appeared clearly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it passed through the ends in about four months, and then I removed the stitches that I had put on the wound, and from one side and the other, and he could not get out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then he did not cease to subtly and ingeniously devise ways of using tools, until I took them well made, according to the form that it will come at the end of this chapter, so that I can treat and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the miracle worker judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I healed it anyway, and the wound was closed, and the pain was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or I told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your skill on what I do not say, because the books cannot contain everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the wise masters compare it to a small thing, and because of what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instrument, in the understanding of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not issue from limbs unless by two methods:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the limb where they enter, or by another part.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which exits by the same way it entered is an arrow that has entered through the bowel, and it has never exited.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not exit, let it remain until the bowel is poisoned and rotten inside, and let it be left to its own issue.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot be removed, let it remain for several days, and move it every day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps out, and if it does not jump out, pierce all around with a thin needle, until the flesh around it is expanded, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the head bone, and goes towards one of the bellies of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have described to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if it is not pulled out, but left until it becomes even after several days, because if the arrow comes towards the face, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not embedded in the bone only, and does not come to the surface, and remains there for several days without any bad event, then the engine of drawing should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if she is very crooked like this and cannot get out, then administer tar, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then heal the limb until it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to the body but cannot be seen, then search for it throughout the tent.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then remove it with any suitable instrument.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if you cannot remove it due to the narrowness of the wound, and the deep penetration of the arrow, and there is no bone or sinew or vein, then leave it until the wound becomes large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and if you find an arrow, and if it has ears attached to it that it holds, then break the shaft where you can, and then break or pull off the ears from the shaft, as much as you can.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully do not break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	If you cannot do it once, if the leg is completely inside the thigh, then cut it off, for the extraction has failed.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding occurs due to this, then follow what we have said about the treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put in place as you can pull out the arrow without danger, or quickly or slowly, or firmly or loosely.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Put the patient according to the shape it was in when the arrow came out, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do so, put it according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, which opens nothing and where the skin is swollen in one place so that it can be seen or felt abnormally:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	Then cut above, as long as the barbs can be taken hold of, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	If it has now sunk in.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then round your hand and push it into the bone, until it enters the bone, and expands the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still and then begin extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is of an arrow and it is, if it is shot through;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if it is poisoned, and you see administer gently, if you administer the instrument chewed, so that the tip of the arrow between the hair of the instrument;
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then bite further, and if the arrow is chewed, if it bites the instrument entering at the point, to alleviate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is lodged, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow is poisoned or painful or in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cover over it, if it covers.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from covering the vein and nerve, and then extract it, and then cut the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and the treatment until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the hooks used to extract arrows resembles an owl's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways to do this:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	large, medium, and small, according to the amount of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the needle is also like the beak of a bird, to pierce at the tip of the blood, like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the needles for pricking and for drawing is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one can bleed, including the main ones, which are 16, namely:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	2 branches that are after the ears, which are called the "two herbs";
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the 2 arteries that are in the two temples appearing;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the 2 veins that are in the two armpits of the two eyes, which are called "aspirates";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is placed in the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is at the back of the head;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugular veins that are on the neck;
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins called "auguste";
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are outside the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that one cuts commonly are V in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	the other is the cervical, and is on the right side, and they call it the "head vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the remedy is called "fasting", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic veins, and they call it the laymen "vein of the heart".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the basilic vein is located on the right side, and they call it the laymen "vein of the belly", and it is above the femoral artery, and it is the one that is used to heal, which opens clearly above the groin.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	and the subclavian vein is the one that is between the auricular and annular artery, and it has two branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg there are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	The first one is dislocated at the left shoulder, and the second one is at the elbow of the right shoulder.
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the vein that is called "nesse", which is in the elbow of the other shoulder.
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg, there are three veins dislocated from those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The sinus of the veins that are after the ears helps with ancient catarrh and headache.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	And the qualities of the sinus, as I said to you, and it is that you reset the head of the pain, and rub the skin where the veins are with a rough cloth.
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	Then compress the hairs on their neck with a bandage until the two veins appear behind the ears in both sides of the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	And if you feel pain on your neck, and if you see the hairs standing up, then stop.
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	Then take the lancet, and place it outside the vein near the bone, then lift your hand above the vein, and cut through the skin and the vein, and it should go straight through the vein until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then stop and tie it until it is healed.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	I have already mentioned the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The cure for the second artery that is in two temples, it is to drain the ancient, and soothe, and harden accustomed, and at the courts of the tears ages to those.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of the skilled healer are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	And it is that the painful one strains his neck, so that both veins appear openly.
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And he feels the hairs on the other side, and then lifts up the eyelid;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	Then lift the finger above the vein on the other side, and prick the lancet outside, and lift the vein up, and cover it, as you have done in the two other veins, and do according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the pain, and put your finger on the wound for an hour, then put on a cloth.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then tie it firmly, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken of them and their treatment and removal, at the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the wound on the forehead is just as valuable as the healing of headache diseases and facial old wounds, and migraine, and a rupture.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the pain twists his neck, until the wound appears.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the tool called "fosser", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the point of it on the vein, and hold it with your hand or something else, and let the blood issue according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then cut away the vein, and tie it until it is secure and no more blood flows out like a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	However, it should not be too tight;
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and the knot on the side, because the bone is close, and by chance the string may break when it is thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The second vein that is in the two arms helps to those, and at the elbow, and at the wrist, and at the shoulder, and at the diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the hairs twist their neck in turning from any direction, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and let the health be through the cross, a little long of the flame a little wide, for there is no harm.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	And if their flames are thin, perhaps they break;
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make bleeding of the blood, as much as you have skill, and then tie with cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The health of the vein of the neck is good for ague, and for sweating, and for diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, and continuously when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the qualities of the pain are such that the hairs tense their neck, then they strain their nostril to your right hand, and take the subtle flame long, and the wick into the space between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well inquire, and the sinus will now begin to heal.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not move too much from there, and treat the blood according to your need, then leave it overnight, because it is quickly restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The pain of the two jawbones helps to narrow the alveolar arch, and at the beginning of mastication, and for many diseases, and pustules, and corrosions, and herpes, and eczema;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the skin is such that the hairs stray from one side to the other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and whether the masters are above the top of the wound, and the wound is on the seat, then clean the vein with a long incision, slightly wide, then draw out the blood frequently, as much as the matter requires.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then make another incision on the other vein, then release the ligature, and hold the wounds steadily, so that the hairs do not strangle.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and let it bleed until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the liver above helps to cool in the mouth, and prevents tooth decay, and cracks in the lips, and dry throat and inside.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the saint is to make the pain sit in front of you, and hold its neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the eyelid, and look at the two veins, one on the right eyelid and the other on the left, and they are known by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that there are small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	then tie both of them, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then tie the largest one from each part, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method:
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The cleaning of the veins that are outside the tongue helps after the cleaning of the cephalic, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the qualities of a good cleaner are that diseases cease between your hands before the sun, and you stretch out your tongue, and look outside at each side a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Therefore clean both and do not go too far in front, for outside are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins of the neck that are cleaned commonly are cleaned in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	when holding onto all the fire with a wide, sharp blade, or like a surgical scalpel, and it is called "anesthesia";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame is very famous, and is as wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And there is skill for opening closed veins that are plainly visible from the outside, and which contain large amounts of blood and are disturbed;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the sharp blade:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtlely pointed, and is for cleaning fine veins, where there is fine blood clots.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are outside the neck, and where the collarbone, and where the chest, and where the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the surgeon to act wisely, and to separate from the artery which is out of place.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and blood gushes out, then it is necessary to apply pressure, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not pinch the flame, but cut as an anvil.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the bishop does not open clearly, then it is necessary to hold and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you want any part of him, or you act in place of the vein in the arm.
elle apert manifestement;	it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and the cup to the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you know the joint of the shoulder, then it is also necessary that you strain the arm, so that you touch the joint until you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the shoulder joint, and then bind the arm, and cup the vein with the flame as before.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	And watch that you do not puncture the artery when you see the joint swelling, for it is of the artery.
eschui la donques.	Then move away from it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it emerge as high as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from the artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hasten then, and place your hand on the length, then press your hand without pause, as many times as it has happened.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	Tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the hairs.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be under fear, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if it is not healed without pain, and you are not present with the medicine, then prick the artery if it opens, for the head of the vein retreats.
et estainche li sans.	Heal the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	Take a piece of cloth, and tear it, and take one half and tie it well to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if they are not stained, it is good;
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if not, then the cure, as we have said, with powders that stain blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stains are not too dark in many positions of the small limb of the wound, and the position of the joint of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The cleansing of the wound in the middle helps that it treats blood from the head above, and from the body below, because it is composed of the basilica and the cephalic, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it is necessary for the cleaner to go through the tendon that is outside, and if not too much in front, and he finds the tendon, and he inflates and the stain is dark, and perhaps it cannot be cleaned.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve is often exposed, and if it does not expose itself in any men due to its subtlety, then you must use the instrument of needles.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and protect the nerve for your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The needle of the cerebral type helps, as it draws out blood from the head, and helps with those.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is best to use a needle in the olive oil or mineral oil lamp, as it is the safest of all veins, because it does not contain any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is best to ask for the lightest limb, and do not cause any harm if you cannot find it the first time, and then restart.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes the shoulder swells in some people, but it is necessary the first time, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you should know about healing is that healing is only intended for keeping health and preventing diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	And the healing is done in one of the three veins that are either cut:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	That is to say, cephalic, median, and basilar.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should heal at the beginning of the first ten days, and in autumn and winter after fasting, when the signs of repletion appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	And one should first cleanse the affected joint or limb after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The cleansing administered for diseases does not have a determined time, but it is best to do so every hour or at night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not necessary to cleanse children under the age of fourteen, nor a pregnant woman except for those in their fourth month up to seven months of pregnancy.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should also not sain the elderly who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wants to cleanse in any way, it is necessary for them to wipe the intestines with a light clyster, if they have too much feces retained, so that the veins do not attract the excess and harmful intestinal contents to the principal limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither does one who is too fond of meats, nor one who is indulgent, become healthy, as much as they may be, nor hydropathic.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if one becomes sick after a bout of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, and frequent pregnancy, childbirth, travel, watching, and fasting, and all the virtue, or by some cause of the arm or body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then subtly the humors, if they are not too thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	Then enter or bathe, if nothing prevents, to thin the blood, and to save you from bleeding too much at the third hour, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from that day of work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be tied and joined, and let the healers be higher than those who heal, and let the rub the arm II times or III, then strain the joint above movement, for if it is too loose or tight, it cannot be corrected;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	then rub the limb with hands, until the veins swell, and feel for them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then drip the healer’s flame from a small amount of old oil, then put their finger on the vein where they want to heal, so that the vein does not burst and fail to bleed.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	Because there are veins that flee as quickly as strings to the scribe, and if there are some that are plain of thinness, so that when one puts above the flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is one of those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow, because it is necessary that the scribe be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if it opens the vein the first time, it is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	but if not, then it should try again a little below that joint or above firmly, if the vein is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	If the joint is swollen, and the hairs sprout, let it rest for one or two days, and do not bind the arm tightly.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perchance I will come to abscesses in the future;
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	do not enter or take a bath, then restart the healing if it pleases.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the wound is small, or if you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you saw, then trust in that wound itself directly to the fire.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and work gently, provided that the joint is swollen;
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swelling, do not begin again with the same bandage, and put on a small amount of oil, for it soothes the pain of the wound, and is quiet in this limb like the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the bandage of oil in each wound that you bandage, to stop the flow of the blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	And this same thing is made into a triangle and a bow, when it is put on the limb.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If subtly the wound and separate it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there comes some large abscesses, which often happen, immediately when it is not bandaged except at this time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry, and put on the limb a soft sponge in boiling water and a little cloth, and hold it an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the removal of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place for several days without any discoloration or greenish tint, then it is not necessary to remove it.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place something of aloe or mire in a juice of calamint, monkshood, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And often there is an abscess and appearance of the sores of the basilica:
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	and then place your hand on it, and if you press the limb gently with your hand, if it is that appearance badly.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	Therefore do not place anything of what we have said, because inadvertently it may cut into the artery.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but apply a dry plaster to strengthen the limb, then use other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the wound.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if it is not black, let it remain out until it becomes red;
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if you see it swollen, let it remain out until it becomes thinned.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is suitable for those who are weak and have skill in extracting arrows, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and let it heal quickly and often, and it should be treated by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	This method of healing is safe from the corrosion of blood and the strangulation of nerves, and it is as good as the healing done over a long period of time or a wide area.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	And to those who need it for the healing, it is appropriate to give bread made from ground grains mixed with apple juice.
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	If it is hot-blooded, then pour out the blood three or four times and if it is of cold complexion, change the bread to bread made from honey syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a strong-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the sweat, after much blood loss, it is appropriate to give him a broth of charcoal, and a subtle-smelling syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the chapter or section on syncope, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to exercise his arm, and strengthen it again, if necessary, when it is weakened by great injury, that he should strengthen it gradually, according to the quantity of its continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he wants to exercise his arm after the first strengthening, and he has strong pain, then he should strengthen it again seven hours after the first strengthening, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he wants to strengthen on the other side, then he should strengthen it again on the second day or the third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	Because he has much blood inside his body which is already heated, and causes fever;
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw a large quantity, and widen the vein as much as possible;
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must meet all the conditions of health, and put your hand on the pulse when it is healthy, so that the patient does not come into the vein in place of the pulse, and this has often happened when the healers are neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and you must not draw blood when you see the arm shaking, and make blood come out the second time, and the vein is closed, that you press firmly on.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, he should extend his arm quickly, for that would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but let it rest until it heals the second time.
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you do not put the tip of the flame on it until the ice that has been frozen from the vein is softened, and put a drop of oil back in its place, and press it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the swelling is present, let it be and do not hold it tightly until the abscess is calmed down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary to draw out blood from the second vein, if the healthy one in the same limb or another arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins are healthy in place of the main vein because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the way of healing is that the hairs put their hand in hot water until the flesh is red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then gently tie it, so that the vein appears well, then heal it now from the side, not too narrow or too long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and let the wounds be wide, and clean well near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand in hot water, and let the blood flow in the hot water, until you have enough;
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is still stuck, do not put the hand back in hot water, because it puts more in than out;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the cleaning of this wound is safer than all other wounds, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cleaning of the wound of the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver, and this is the way:
