estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strain the hand, and apply hot water, until the vein is blown, if one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the wound is crooked, and if you cover it with all kinds of things, it will not hurt anything.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not move too much in the beginning, because the nerves are all exposed to the flesh, and then put the hand in hot water again, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the arrow as much as is necessary for you, put oil on the wound and tie it with a thread quickly, and thus do to each one.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healthy sign of the left hand is valuable for the disease of the mouse, and do everything as I have told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The healthy sign of the shoulder is valuable for all diseases that are outside the body, such as marrow diseases, and retention of urine, and disease of the knees, and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of its wound is such that the hairs boil in hot water, and rub on the vein until it dies, and tie over the joint of the hair.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and if the vein is at the elbow, and from above the wrist they go much with rain.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then the larger or more open rain, or at the elbow, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it above the wrist, then guard against the nerves that are displaced, and heal it as in sewing.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and let the flames be close.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot issue from the bone, put the flesh in the hot water, and let the wound well drain.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if you have to heal it the first time, then start the second above a little, because the bones are salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	and do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so make the other sewing of the wrist equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein of the ankle is at the knee of the foot, and its healing is equal to the pain of the back, when it is for an abscess.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that the hairs between or in the bath, and strange above the knee four times in twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, then the healthy one in all ways that you can, and crosswise.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	It is worthwhile to hold it, for the veins are dry, and it is very replete with hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not hold it, then the healthy one none of those who open or do two small ones, and towards the small one, and keep away from the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	And make so much correction of the blood that you see, and then release the ligament, and put on cotton and hold it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	It is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of suction wounds
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuums are made of horn, or of brass, or of glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	And vacuum is done in two ways:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this vacuum that is without striking is done in two ways:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	Either it is at all heat, or without heat.
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	And the vacuum that is done by striking and drawing blood is made in twelve places on the body, of which one is at the top of the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	And the others are at the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and two others in two ribs on the shoulder;
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the suction of the face;
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the suction of the two shoulders;
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the suction on the buttocks;
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and the suctions in the two arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and the suctions in the two legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and the suctions in the two knees;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the suction does not treat blood, but only the small veins that are scattered in the body, and therefore it does not weaken the person, as one does with the treatment of bloodletting.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should only be administered when there is no fire or fever, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if necessary for illnesses, it is advisable to ventilate, or by custom, to reset every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in every season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they have business to ventilate, have heavy heads.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if some have fullness and redness in their face, and head, and neck, and darkness before their eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and some who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit out blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are some who dream, and see through red and black and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is in the month of May, we command them to fast for three hours after midday.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The remedy for the pain of the muscles helps with the grieving of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is only suitable after the evacuation of all the blood from the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And this ventilation is in the place of the remedy for the headache, and it is only suitable for those who are of cold constitution or who have diarrhea, because that causes great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And therefore it is not suitable for those who are awake or who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often feel ill, become forgetful, and therefore it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower due to the doubt of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the neck is in place of the remedy for the headache and the basilica, and therefore it is suitable for the narrowing of the vein of the pomum, and for all, and for repletion.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should not be placed too tightly, for if it is held too firmly, it may cause injury to the intestines or stomach and the abdomen.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the second rib of the spine can cause pain in the neck, and numbness and tingling, and choking, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is in the place of the health of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is necessary to command the healer to express his hand when placing it, so that he does not press the artery, and does not cause blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The ventilation of the lower jaw can cause illness in the mouth, and corruption of the teeth, and similar diseases that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the joint of the lower lip.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the shoulders cause disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The wounds of the ears are as valuable as three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	And the patient is instructed not to be too eager in front, for the veins are bare of flesh and can be easily damaged by needles and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The wound on the back above the hips is as valuable as many diseases, and it should be large and made of iron, so that it can draw well.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	And if it were too thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	And I make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The bandages of the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and cause ancient pains of rain, and of the marsh, and of the bladder, and remove the flows;
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	And they are in the place of the second metatarsal bones, and of the second metacarpals, and at all times they weaken the body after long use, and bring on numbness in many positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The way to apply the bandage is that you first put it empty and quickly fill it with heat, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the red and swollen flesh, and open the pores of the blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then, firmly, and reset the suction cups, and take care in the positioning of the vessels, for there are such that have tarry bile, and clear porous ones.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	If it is necessary to prick once only, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and one deep one.
et suce legierement.	And clean lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if it is not too large, then it is necessary to prick twice.
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to thin the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if it is not very sharp, then it is necessary to prick the third time.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And when we want to draw out a little blood at a time, then we should only suck once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we wish to draw much blood, we recommend frequently.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And if the blood is thick, we recommend using a sharp, pointed knife, and it is suitable for those who have thick skin and are tough, that you use the tips of oil-appetizing and dissolving:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in this state, of blue oil, or of almond sweet oil, or of cucumber seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in a feverish state, of celery oil, or of lily, or of chamomile, or another similar one.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or balm, or aniseed oil, and the likes.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one who is to be bled has wide and open pores, then one should not put any oil, but rather wash after the venesection of high rosewater, or high cold water, or myrtle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar thing.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, if they rise from ash, or high myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have excessive swelling rise from old wine, or vinegar of sucking, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and do not wait too long to apply a suction device before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two;
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep immediately after suction, and it is good that they wait until they are ready to be sucked and when they are being sucked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch out for those who are suctioned if they are feverish, and if they are not too weak and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	if it is good that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuces at the outlet, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and muddy puddles, and hot water from a cauldron, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold complexion, take honey syrup, and aromatic wine between old and new, and a little broth, and muddy puddles, small birds, and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day that he will travel, he must drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give some men triangular or muscat wine before traveling, or after, for the benefit of the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And it should be subtly given to the sick, but only those who are strong drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	Vacuum cups applied to cause pain are those placed over the liver, and over the mouse, and podagra, and over the belly and the buttocks and the thighs and the back, for these members do not suffer pain from other methods, and no one does this except to draw blood from member to member, as we place them over the breasts when the child is born;
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place vacuum cups over the belly and the buttocks to soften the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and remove the pain when there is an abscess or stone, as by its attractive virtue it may chance to remove the abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	And thus, when placed over the liver and the mouse, where there is a suction retained, these suctions are administered empty for sweat alone.
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	And never are administered together with fire, and sometimes plain of hot vinegar, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in such a way that the suction is filled with hot steam or hot water where he has cooked poisonous herbs to it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the vacuum administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it has two large and half-palm of length, and it is or costed around the middle I small perforation, as to put a needle, and it is of brass, sulfur before so that it does not bleach the painful part when placing it on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And in the middle of it, use a crooked rod of iron or iron, to put a splint in place, and they should be large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For infants' suction cups are different from old ones, and thin ones are different from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should put this suction cup on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	with a wax splint or linen, and put it in the suction cup at the end of the iron rod that is in the suction cup, so that it clarifies whether the suction cup is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the hairs.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	Then place it above the member, and you should hold it above the perforation that we have said, so that when one wants to, then the suction can go in and one removes the vacuum.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And take hold of the lineament as before, and repeat it often, if you have skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there is no needle or perforation, and it is not administered until it is full of sharpness, and it is placed above the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Nostrils are not administered until in members where one cannot place suctions for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and when removing from a horse, such as a donkey or mule, and other similar cases;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is such that when you thrust through those that are in fresh waters without a net, then take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them into fresh water until they are familiar and have nothing in their bellies;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	then wash them with blood and suction, then rub the limb until it is red, and put on the gut;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are smooth and cooked, if it is a place where a suction can be put, then put it, for this is very good.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, then lift the limb gently, first from above, very well, and then wipe it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if it is too sore after the course of the wounds, then moisten the linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the wound is cleansed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds multiply, then place on broken glass, or salt, and similar things, until it is cleansed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you place on the limb half of crushed beans, and leave them until they dry on the limb, it will stop now.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you have more troublesome ones, take other remedies.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the remedies do not want to take effect, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you make a needle until it enters the wound, and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are stuck, powder on a little aloe and brimstone or ash, and they will now fall off.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, foolish boy, that the false miracles of this chapter were never seen in any of the old books, neither were they letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason, knowledge is lacking in our land, for I found none good.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing, except for the knowledge gained from ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated it, and by experience, and by the habit of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that will be brought, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or preface of this book the sums of the language and the chapters where the wise put their understanding, and dwell on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or wound comes to any one, it is necessary for you to hasten to clean the injury on both sides, if nothing stops you, such as weakness of body, or children, or old people;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	When the joint is not very warm or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and if the joint is not very warm or too cold; and if you drink cold water, such as cold juices, and char of quail and partridge, and do not drink any thick soups, and do not eat too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of an abscess or spreading of matter to the limb;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the hairs regrow as they used to before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to grind the meat that causes large swelling, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and pie, and pancakes of milk, and eggs, and fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the grinding, it is better to do it sooner rather than later.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of old people and the infirm cannot be well healed or joined according to their nature due to the scarcity of flesh, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but do not care, reset it over the broken bone and large thick tendons that stretch and join the limb together, as much as it can bear, until it is as strong as before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not leave it entirely to its own devices, and because it needs to be nourished with large amounts of food, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go around, and others in soaking, like the shape of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture all in a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And in every way, it should have its own intention and proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory brings to its mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that the bone is broken because the joint is twisted, and open wide by default, and it is pressed by the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twisting in his arm, and the hairs do not cause great pain, if there is no fracture;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but he may still have twisting, or a wound, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but place the remedies that come after this, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And if the fracture that goes in the arm is in two parts, and the two parts are dislocated, now you must put them back evenly, as well as abscesses that come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses come, if he leaves no pus, until the abscesses are calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then put it back in the muscle that you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restoration of those where he has pieces.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then the strain, as it should be afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken into pieces, then strain it with two parts, whether by hand or foot, or at your hand if it is small members, or at two strings, or with one string and at your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then reset all the additions in their places at once with your hands, and guard that by your work no harmful injury or pain comes.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and firmly set the two bones according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And if it feels good to the hand, if it seems not quite right.
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if it is stretched well, and not strained too much, and does not press as those who do so often cause abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is set, well restrain the bad movement that it does not move, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and watch well that the limb is so assured that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels no pain, it is not quite set, and it should be put in the best position so that it feels no pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is placed correctly, as twisting can occur when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The members broken are different in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For there are small members, such as fingers and toes and similar ones:
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	so it is necessary to wrap them with soft, thin linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are large, such as the thigh and leg:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	so it is necessary to wrap them with a wide, sturdy cloth, because the large limbs encompass the whole member and evenly strain all parts, so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then lightly press the joint, three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand a little on the entire limb, then go above the fracture and hold it less than the fracture;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and gradually soften the limb a little and little, until you grip a large part of the sound limb, then take another limb and turn around directly above the broken limb;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then return to the part beyond the fracture and hold it gently, neither too strongly nor too firmly, as we have said in the first part above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the lips of linen or cloths, as long as they are even, then tie all together with a bandage, and then put your well-made stitches above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing on the abscess and that which opens the swelling, and leave it like that for some time.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then strain above your stitches, and they should be half of a wide strip, or of bark that is properly cut, or of palm fronds, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but the stake that one puts across the fracture should be slightly larger and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and it should also be as long as needed for the limb, whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then pull across the stakes as you did in the first chapter, then tie it evenly with a thread, just like in the first chapter over the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is pulled, the less there is.
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it should be that the thread is of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of flax.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in some works of fools who make cords from linen that are too thickly twisted, and this is great error, because the band cannot be even if it is too thin, and it should only be that there is less than a finger's breadth between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the hairs are pricked by the thorns after straightening them in their natural position, then soak them in linen or some other clean cloth, so they do not become inflamed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bone fractured, and the bones are broken, I will tell you the treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain all the broken limbs at once on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, one should not put bandages immediately, but after five days or seven, or more according to your safety from abscess, constantly watching.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and now the manner of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and you take flour that is kept in the walls of the mill, and knead it with abundant water, and put this mixture, not too clear or too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring fractures to many positions, and especially to women and small children, because it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another way of applying plasters to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take equal parts of aloe, dandelion, and nail polish, and add 10 grams of Arabic gum and myrrh.
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	myrrh and aloes, 5 grams each;
alechil VIIII З.;	aloe, 8 grams;
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and grind them into powder, and mix with enough honey;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the patient's complexion is hot, then use this plaster, as it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of splinting that is useful for sprains:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	Take a piece of cloth and soak it in warm water, then apply it to the affected area.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	Mix equal parts of honey and aloe, then apply it to the affected area.
acaice VI З.;	Apply a cold compress to the affected area.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Boil equal parts of armagnac and honey, then grind them well and mix with either vinegar or a lot of egg yolk, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another method of splinting for joints and bones that have been dislocated from their sockets, to relieve pain and promote healing, and to prevent further injury.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take a new piece of cloth, soak it in warm oil, and place it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal immediately, but it is good for alleviating abscess pain, and properly relieves the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method to treat broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dried fig leaves and earth partridge leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of healing a broken bone and to ease the remaining pus of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take valerian root, chamomile, flowers of violets, and flour of each one in equal parts.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Grind and mix with wine, and if the limb is hot, apply the mixture with wet or dry coriander seed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of healing more than the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take valerian root, linseed, balm, mallow, and willow bark, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each in equal parts.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	And bruise, and cook with sharp salt, or sweet salt, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, except for a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, things dry and slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another way to treat injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take the hooves and feathers of birds, or pen-feathers, and sage, and silk equally, and bruise them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then remove it after a while, and be careful that the pain is not gone, nor has the bone of its limb become soft.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	If not, remove it by hand later.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, feeling of restlessness or swelling, then you hurry, and remove it, and take off the bandage now.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take light bandage, and wet sponge from the sea, and soak in vinegar, and raise the limb, until the itching stops, and let the pain be relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moisten with vinegar or rose oil, and tie with a bandage, until you are sure of no abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and reduce the inflammation of the limb, and let the pain be removed, then start again with the thin bandage, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and carefully as they are clean.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is filled with pus and redness and pain and swelling, and you have the skill of plasters and liniments, then restart it as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if it does not come to the limb of what we have said within three days or four or five or seven;
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for twenty days, as we see, until the fractured part becomes straight, and approaches the proper position of the bone above;
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then the splint is applied more than before, and the flesh increases in size, as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the limb becoming too dry, there can be no healing;
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then apply a hot, wet cloth every time you remove the splint, and this should be done each day, and release the bandage a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	For this work, therefore, cuts the broken bones in the limb, and quickly heals what the foolish people do, which twist the limb painfully:
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	It is evil, and this work is not worthy of praise, and I see no other thing than pain and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many kinds of fractures are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	because it has fractures that are made by the percussion of a sword, and the collarbone is broken completely through the bone, which is outside the bone, as it is cut or broken;
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, it is called by this name of fracture "haiture".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Where the spear pierces the bone from above, and is called by this name of fracture "absolute".
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and is the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion from above, or cutting or from the neck of the spear, or to fall on the stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if he has a broken bone that approaches the skin, which is outside the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is set in the bone as thin as a hair, and is the fracture small, and for this reason, it is called by this name of fracture "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	And if the wound that is made by being pierced by an arrow, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and is the threads like when they hammer nails into the kitchen ceiling when they hammer above.
si entre li piere dedens.	if between the stones inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And they have more in those who have or wet bones, as in children.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	And they have all these ways of fracture that small pieces are removed as these.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	And I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breaking by pulling on them, and by the inspection of tented parts, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hairy part is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed with it, if there is an open black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, be careful of accidents of evil, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes to issue forth and redden, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes first to you, and it is in the bone, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day or you will not be able to.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the soft tissue, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin over the bone is not rotten, and the injuries that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then you must remove the broken part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and it is that you hold the head of the painful wound, and reveal under the bone in all ways that you can, and above the shape of the wound as soft as you can, and if blood comes to discover the bone, or abscess, help with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the place with moist linen cloths in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calm, and be sure of the cessation of bleeding;
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin around the bone to cut, and it is done according to the two methods of surgery:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	one method is that you cut at a narrow incision in front, and it is this form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	and the second method is that you have many different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed and made of iron outward;
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and in working lightly, that you do not wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the tooth is very hard and firm, it is necessary that you first drill around it, as long as you have tools with tapers, not before it passes through the bone, and it should have above the point a margin or a circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone;
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and you should have several, so that each one fits in its place of the bone's spine, so that you have tools for all teeth;
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three kinds of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality for drilling around the bone is that you place the drill on the bone, and turn it to your right until you feel that the bone is drilled through;
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then apply the sharp object on the other side a little later, and so do everything around, then carefully cut the space between the bones that is between the joints, and do it more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you remove the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools you have such as forceps, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is advisable to open the space that remains of the bone to all other tools similar to a scalpel, but it is necessary that it be more tenacious and more subtle than the other scalpel.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	And if he does not remove any of the small bones or scales, gently remove them with the instruments.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	Then treat the wound with bandages and ointments that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And the other method of work is as follows, which the Gauls mention, which is safer;
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and the loan is very strong, and that is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you remove a part of the bone where the break is open, so that when you have exposed that part, you can place the lens shape of this eyelid, which is why it is shaped like this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut a small piece, and it is the party age in two parts, so that the cutters are towards the bone;
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then hold a small hammer above, so that you gently cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is against the bone, then gently, because one can harm it by force, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, then it is necessary to remove those sharpness, and to scrape off the scales with the fine razor that you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb in the most convenient way, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If before large razors, and then more subtle ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	In each of the other haircuts and delicate cuts, it is necessary to adjust according to its position.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	And this is something that cannot be answered by him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is exposed, then it is necessary to apply a piece of linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and rub it with rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	Then take another piece of cloth doubled in two or three, and rub it with wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and do it more gently than you can, so as not to wound the sciatic nerve, then administer by above and another limb, and do not strain it until it stains the wound only.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and let it stay there for one or two days until the abscess is soothed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of mastich, frankincense powder, aristolochia, and similar things;
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and of these things make a powder, and put on the wound, and administer common medicines without bitterness.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	And ensure that the wound is clean, so do not leave any dirt on it, nor allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers on the brain's surface, it causes great harm.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when one places a sharp object on the wound, do not pull it out from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents occur, as we have said, then it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if there is no other remedy available except the one placed on the wound, then it is necessary to apply a piece of cloth soaked in honey, three parts of rose oil, and one part of gauze, and place it on the wound.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the care of various cures that are suitable, until they are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	That sometimes both parts of the jawbone above are broken, or one by itself, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	And that one is cartilaginous and does not break easily, if it does not twist or dislocate, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must bend your little finger or thumb into the jawbone, and put the break inside your index finger, and at the pouch by default, until the jaw regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this carefully, and ensure that the hairs do not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the broken part is in the part above the nail, and cannot reach the finger, then it is necessary that you place it at the top of a small bone.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the fracture is of two parts, then make another, and hurry to restore the first one, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the abscesses have subsided, then apply a head bandage of linen cloths to the affected area, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	Or you apply another on the other side, where the fracture is.
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and they should be thick enough to fill the gaps in the skull.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no one said how to boil the tents in water, and to kill each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be pounded in the making of an ointment from egg yolk and powdered linseed.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	Then leave the tent, until the bones are iron and the cartilages hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never use feathers or goose down in place of tents, and if the patient has a headache, wrap it around, and hold the breaker, and blow the pains through.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Or do what you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working, put a piece of cotton or a cotton swab in rose oil or a drop of iodine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if there are no boils, put on plaster made of senna flour, and powdered frankincense, mixed with an ointment from egg yolk, then put on light bandages, and do not bind too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bone of the nose is broken into small pieces, and it is broken into smaller pieces, then extract them with appropriate tools, then cut off the fracture, and the cure of things in jarring char, and suture, as emplastres and ointments suitable for it.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound in the nose, then the cure of tents, and put on bandages until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured without an open wound, and the break is not complete but only partially, and it is not broken in two pieces, but rather bent inside, if one knows this clearly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right part, that you bite your index finger into the wound;
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left jaw, then bite your index finger of the right hand, and bite the fracture lightly inside, and press it with the other hand by default, and put even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is displaced in two pieces, it is necessary that you administer traction of two parts until it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if movements of the teeth occur, or fracture, then strain them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place on the broken jawbone, and place over it a double cloth.
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And place over it a great well-made pad or a piece of evenly cut leather, long and wide according to the jawbone, and tie it to the muzzle so you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, then release the animal from the trap, and then put it back in place what is changing.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	And apply plaster on it, with enough flour or semolina of wheat after you have removed the broken jawbone.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and place the lighter plaster on top of it, and if the plasters stick together, do not change the position of the injury, let it remain until it is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come, as we have said many times, apply what we have advised.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is a fracture and wound together, stitch no part of the bone that is broken;
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	so subtly from the bone as to avoid instruments of evil.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it as needed by fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, clean the wound if it is wide, and apply uncovenable plasters to that end, to stop bleeding until they are healed.
de la forcele	of the elbow
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The shoulder is broken more than once in front and behind, and the fracture is in three ways:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and disjointed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the least difficult to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	where there has been a break with wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work if it is regarding the break with wound, that you have two assistants, one of whom feels the force of the broken bone;
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the other extends the neck towards the affected part;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then set the break to your two, so that it is as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you have to extend further, put a round, padded shoulder cushion of cloth or other material, and it should be large according to your need;
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and hold the shoulder steady, and hold the bone in your hand, so that you can set the fracture properly, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder downwards, because it comes out in front, then it is necessary that the painful parts be gently moved up and down over their place, and place something under the shoulder, a moderately sized earthenware jar, and push up the shoulder until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then apply your fingers to the fracture, and if you feel any movement, it is necessary that you cut through it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and carefully trim the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but do not use this instrument on the shoulder to guard against infection:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it resembles a spoon, and is not very sharp, and should be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the workman.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	And say "Two shoulder blades, one broad and the other narrow, as you see, and like the edge of the wound that you made when you treated the bones;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are sure of the abscess, if the wound is large, and if the edge is small, or if you doubt the abscess, use the wound with cloths and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it is heated, soak the cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is painful and when it is cut, is that you place above the bone the plaster of the mill powder and some salt, and put light dressings on it, and put a needle outside the wound, if you have the skill;
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	Then take a very large bandage from the palm of your hand in width, then put it double over the wound and the plaster;
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin strip of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down;
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and put the strip across the broken bone, and wrap the bandage over the neck, and unbind the healthy side, and unbind the injured side;
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the bandage is holding the broken bone evenly, and you see clearly that the strip does not move over the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the bandages are loosened, then restrain them;
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	Let the misaligned limb lie on its back, and place a small pebble under the joint when it is asleep to help lift the dislocation.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	If the fracture of the humerus is aligned by the alignment of the shoulder, or if you bind the arm to the neck, and the dislocation does not return within 20 days.
