puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	Then restart the splint if you see that there is still a need, and hold it in place until it is fully restored.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	It is restored within 28 days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or is dislocated from its place, and it only occurs when it is touched.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if the shoulder bone according to the figure of the break, and the joint is reset according to its natural form, in all ways that you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then put on the limb powder from the mill with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and put it on a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	then put on a wide and thin splint, a little larger than the shoulder, and see that the splint does not touch any part of the shoulder, so use the hair of bandages of linen, so that the splint is evenly soaked.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then restrain it with a strong, tight bandage, so that the dislocated joint does not move from its place, and look at each joint every day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it is dislocated again, restrain and straighten it if it is out of its place, and press the painful parts against its side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is restored in 20 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if it dislocates again, and be careful, for it is not bones that move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is sticking out before, and not removed immediately, then cutting it off, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the mallet to relieve an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the hammer
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The bone is never broken in the middle, but this rarely happens.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks again.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it leans to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no relief, and everything, and possibly vomiting blood, and the jaw is open in the broken bone, and the patient feels very ill.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is that the misaligned bones are often pushed back into place above their own position, and the shoulder is placed between the shoulder blades, then the shoulders are pressed, and the ribs of the two ribcages are held in your hands, and subtly put back into all the positions you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be;
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	then put plasters and wet cloths above the broken bone of salt, or another light one, and wrap it in a bandage, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move;
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	And turn the joint roundly to the back, and steadily press, and warm every hour the book, and if it dislocates again, press.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	And if it is necessary to remove, for corrosion or for pruritus that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, then hurry and remove it, and apply the ointment, and address what has come from methods of treatment.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reset the ointment, and press until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	Know that the breaker of ribs comes only in the large ones after the back, and at the top inside, and does not break unless because they are brittle.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and the smell is not good at the incision.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and splint it with a splint, if you know how to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the ribs are broken and displaced inward, the pain is very great, and pointed, like that of tears, because the bones pierce the flesh.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And there is a lot of blood, and everything is swollen, and there is great pain, and the old ones put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the stomach, to push the broken bone out of place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this mistake, unless there is no pus if it has not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they said none of those who put suction cups on the limb, to draw out evil, and that is similar to reason.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	However, doubt and because the suction cup does not draw out the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that no one should cover the limb with linen dipped in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to even out the lung around it, then treat the care of pleurisy, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the pain is great that he cannot bear it due to the bone that does not support it, and there is doubt, then you must cut above the broken rib on the side, and you must place a remedy to protect the wound.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then you must drill the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	And if abscesses come from the feet, then place moistened linen cloths on red oil, and put on the limb.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	et cure while the limb that is necessary for an abscess, and let it lie flat on its side or as it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No time comes when the fractured bone of the neck breaks, and rarely does it rain;
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if they will be healthy or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is often deadly in many conditions, and if they move and feel well when you press on them, but not when you do not, it means that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are healed, if they are treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healed or not, take notice if the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in hand are as they should be, and on the back there is a sensation of emptiness and evacuation without volition;
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And when placed on their back, they involuntarily expel feces.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is laid on its back and it wants to sit up, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	It is deadly:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	If not treated properly.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to it, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is to reward if there is an abscess that is very painful, and put oil of rose or chicken grease on it, until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	Then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bandage it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And do not sleep on that side where he feels the pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	And if any bone becomes dry, it is necessary to cover it with oil.
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then crush the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, at a seam, then apply the healing ointment with charcoal, until it is healed.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	And if the bone fracture is called "the key of the knee", then take your fist with your right hand and place it evenly on the other hand to your power, then apply the plaster and the splint, if you have skill.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then strap it, and if there is a dry bone, then crush it and the bone, and heal the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs in the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if it does, it is not due to a slight decrease in the neck.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	And making it long, and inclining to the side, and coming to the bone, causing pain, swelling, and inflammation where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over, as high as the fractured part.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	And saws off what is broken and its shape.
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And if the break is only at the head, then put it back in place until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inward, then make the patient lie on their back until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have set it even, place the ointment on top, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the broken part still so it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and apply pressure to the sides until the bone is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess forms and comes, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed down, and then follow what we have previously said.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to the resetting, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident.
et c’est li maniere.	And that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The assistants are what is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	one is that you take a piece of gristle, in this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and tie the two ends to the two joints, and let them hang up high, and cut off the evil above the seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the broken arm over the stump, until it comes to ease, and has in its midst a piece of wood, then let it hang over any heavy thing or the assistant extends it down;
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Then place the broken bones evenly in the hands together, until the broken bone returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one should prick the hairs above their temple, and then hold the patient's hand on their collarbone, then command two ministers to have one tug on the part that is above the broken bone at their hands, and the other tug outside of everything, and stretch each one to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the patient's limb outside of everything, and above the broken bone, and stretch each one of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the broken bone is near the top of the shoulder, it is necessary to place the middle bone away from the shoulder, and the other towards the back, away from the broken bone;
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	And similarly, if the broken bone is towards the back, it is necessary to place the middle bone gently, with effort, until the broken bone is even on the shoulder, and on the back;
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	Then place the break evenly, as it should be, and hold it still, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it for less than seven days, and put milk and red oil on it until the abscess is soothed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you put the plaster on the broken part, then bring the arm up with the shoulder joint, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and put the bandage, and hold it with the shoulder joint, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something prevents it, or if the bone does not move.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, and have two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes three fingers on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	Then strain against the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more strongly and less in pulling them away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you see the position of the splints and the straining, as we have said in the chapter where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is healed, leave it to be tied after seven days, as we have said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine every three days the joint that itches and does not come to the skin, or the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accidents come, then wait for three days or more, and let the pain lie on his back, and have his hands on his stomach;
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and put a bandage of flax evenly on the dislocation, and examine every hour of the day or night, that the appearance of the limb does not move, or the joints are not softened;
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if the pain increases by the power of medicine, and the meat that we have put before, in such a way that the meat is at the first subtle;
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	When he begins to recover, if he is large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in 10 days after all.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And then you must apply ointments and medicines to the limb to promote healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If its structure is ugly and swollen, it may take 1 month or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "humerus" and radius, one of which is smaller and is the one that forms the elbow.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	And the other is larger and is the one that is outside, next to the small one.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	Perhaps the large bone is broken alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	And when the large bones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then it should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is the large bone, then it must be stretched more forcefully;
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it over the cushion, and tuck the palm of the hand higher than the others, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the pains cross each other over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the pains suffer no labor.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	then extend the assistants one arm to the part below their hand, or to their elbow, and other assistants to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he puts the mirror evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no way to hold the bone together, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the bleeder, I have spoken of it in the chapter alone;
si pren la cure.	if take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if in the beginning of restoration there are abscesses, then use the cloth of cerate made of red oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft;
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and tie the cloth gently, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	And then remove the cerate, and put the poultice of flour from the mill with plenty of honey, then put the stars, and let the star of the bleeder stick more outside, and a little wider than the others;
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and it should have six or more arms in many positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	whether the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two:
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and held above the breaker more than on the other side, and always less in moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter:
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and let the cloths that are above the breaker be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp:
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and let the thread that it is held with be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the member and the limb after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if any evil accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must raise the member in hot water, until those itching are appeased:
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and allow the limb to remain at ease.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then restart the restriction, and if the limb is broken and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, then advise.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the bruises cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and leave it like that for some days, until the bruises have healed, and then restrict.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If none of these things we have said come to pass, then do not delay in seeking help for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	or apply it around, then place his hands on his neck, and make his neck even, and avoid movement and jarring, and sleep on his back;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and that this fracture is restored in thirty days or thirty-five, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and constitutions of its virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wait until the back of the hand and as we have said before, there are few fractures, and it does not come but many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly in front of him.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then place his hand on the extended palm, and extend the bones broken by the minister, and put them evenly in their places until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no abscesses, then put an estele according to the amount of the limb;
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is at the parched ends within the sole of the foot, then make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken foot.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then strain it with a long cloth, and let the estele of cow's udder be as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the forearm, it is necessary to place one splint above and another below the hand, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it completely around the arm, and stitch the ligament between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if the fracture comes to any of the other fingers, if it is the thumb, then put it evenly, as needed.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and the restriction with the plant, and if you see that put a straight small stake to lift the broken part, and it does not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the broken part is like other joints, such as the index or another, then put it even, and tie it with the healthy joint that is next.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you tie them all together, as much as possible, or you put on a stake, like a splint.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and in the positioning of abscesses, and support what comes to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken rib
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The jaws of the mouth are often broken, and well seen when it returns in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when one joint is placed above the broken part, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the bones are set back into place, then each minister attaches their joint to its equal part evenly.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the break is placed in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is close to the root of the rib cage, then one of the ribs should be on top of the other, and the other ribs outside the broken part.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And if it is near the hip, and then the joints below the hip are stretched downwards.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then place the bone equally in both hands, as it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bandage, and if there are no complications, it will heal.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is an abscess, let it calm down first, then return to your work and care.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The leech is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	It is necessary to wrap the broken bone in a bandage doubled over two or three times, and leave the excess, then bend the leg until the toes reach the root of the heel, and insert a long thread between the calf and the leg, below the knee joint, and bring the end of the thread to the top.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then bend over the leg and the calf, then place the bandage on the broken bone, and place a splint on the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then place the patient's leg between soft cloths to maintain equal traction, then begin to twist about three or four times over the fractured bone.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	And as you go higher than the fracture, and lessen the traction.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	Then bring the two ends of the rope that you have tied between the leg and the thigh, and tie three knots on top, then return to the other end of the rope, until you come over the knee.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And maintain the traction, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, then when there is no infection or swelling or any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it has happened, then dislocate, and straighten what comes, as we have said many times.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are pieces of bone that can be felt, then try to put them back if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it cannot be put back, then cut the limb and draw out the bone.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never break the ribs in such a way that they are put back, as in the dislocation and shoulder.
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Nevertheless, in this restoration made thus, it does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is said that the bone is restored at different times, according to the variety of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the way of the gentleman
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the way of the gentleman, there is little breakage, but it often weeps.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a small cut, or a puncture, and it has to all wounds, and without wound, and it feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when one puts back together what was broken to its proper place, as much as it can be assembled when it is put together.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the poultice, and if you have skill, use a round bandage, and treat it as it should be, then warm all the arrangements that we have said in other broken things, such as abscesses and similar things.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And for each accident, put what it needs, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Be aware that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "non-mustelz", and the other is called "foscile".
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And it can break in any direction as it comes to the arm, and for this reason, the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg from all parts returns.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then it heals in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain, and it can be seen clearly.
et torne desoz.	And it returns disjointed.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	Therefore, first relieve the extension, and put it back in place, and tie the tendons equally;
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but anyway, it is necessary that the broken part be straight, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is less and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and the herb according to its virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your work, take four strips of cloth that encircle the leg on one side and the other, and be long from the knee to the groin on both sides.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	Then wrap the four strips of cloth above and below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this point it will not allow the leg to bend to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	And no one administers the long strip of cloth down the leg, and it is made of flax, and place the leg to prevent movement, and properly made, one puts it in the break or where there is a wound.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	And move each leg daily to see if there is an abscess or other accident.
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if the healer is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fractures
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but of bone fractures, it never comes and it is rare, and there are no other dispositions except for a slight bruise in some cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if he has broken bones, and you see the bones over each other, if you put your foot on the ground like it wants to walk, then put your foot on his, where the bones are lifted, then press until they return to their place.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then put the poultice and soak above the foot, and put a small tablespoon of the remedy on the sole of the foot, then strap it to the foot evenly, then wrap bandages around it and other things you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if you relocate the joint, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	If there are any of the two broken, restore them as we have said about the two fingers;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place the broken one on the length of the other, and make it a bit wider, then place the bone in the hole that I mentioned, and strain it evenly;
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three or more broken, place each one on the length of the other, wrapped in a piece of linen, and strain the hole from outside the bone;
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and make sure it is on the top of the table away from the belly of the bone, so that it heals well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and treat each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the jaw of a woman is broken, if the fracture is enlarged, then incline it to the side of the neck, and hold it in place from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	Then fill the hollow of the jaw with cotton, and put in as much as you can.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	Then raise the woman, and slowly lift her back, and then quickly remove the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the jaw, and the bone returns with the cotton.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	When she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, return it, and thus do this for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	If she is healed from the fracture, and if you see, take a catheter of birch, and tie a string to the handle, and fill the entire catheter with urine in its natural state.
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	Then blow into the string until the catheter is empty inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	The natural state will return to the fracture.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then it should be filled with cotton and left in this way for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when the tooth of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and his use to it, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture signifies many positions of the right way of resetting:
enten le donques.	therefore understand it.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	In the finger, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the finger;
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	then wrap it with cloths, and leave it for three days or more, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of broken with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a broken bone with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleansed immediately, so that the cleansings that we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if the wound is dressed with vitriol, if you have no other means, then begin to restore the broken bone in the same hour or the next day, before the wound becomes infected.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the wound becomes infected, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the infection is calmed, and do not touch it on the following day or the fourth, for you will bring about bad events.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the teeth are broken and appear above the gum line, it is necessary that you gently place them in your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if you are not able to equalize your hands with this extension tool, which is made of iron and has seven or eight inches of length, and the width is according to the amount of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because it is necessary for the mirror to take three or four, according to how much it has in each fracture treatment.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and slightly thick, so that it does not press too much on the member at your work, and it should be thin behind, and thick in the middle in front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	And it is called "palainche", because it should be placed on the top of the head of the visible bone.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and the cup is once, as much as it can, evenly placed against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone until the instruments have hold.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then use an appropriate instrument for this purpose, such as a saw or scissors, to your ability;
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then cut away what is remaining in the bone of harshness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned to its place, and the pain is great afterwards, advise that it not remain in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	If you do this until it is in its place, then wipe off the blood with black vinegar wine, and properly if it was in this state;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not place anything on the wound except for cerate or other things where there is oil, that it does not cause putrefaction and corruption;
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer these ointments when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover the dressing all around, according to the size of the wound, and take care that the wound is not pressed with the break.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and many times have done this by the foolish man, and brought the pain or death or corrosion never.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and let the astringents be softer and more gentle than other wounds.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt whether a bad accident has not occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain to the limb, then it does not matter to put on ointments.
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but around, in place of stones, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after an hour or two that the bleeding has stopped, remove what you have placed on top of everything, and put healing ointment on the wound, such as quadruple antifarmacological ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to clean the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be aligned in such a way that the bow can move freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to exceed, and it cannot be sutured but remains dislocated, there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you tear the wound with a tent, and remove all those unnecessary pieces that cause that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or another way of corruption, then it is necessary that you treat it, according to what it says in its chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when the bone is broken and open above the member, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large members, do not pull it out, for many times it causes death, but let it be until it can be fixed.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	perhaps it will fall out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of sudden blows that come to the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	Many times after the healing of the broken bone, specifically when it is near the joint, and the unpleasant thing is to see the shape of the member.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	And by chance, cannot do their natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Take then, since it is fresh:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	If you administer medicines that are styptics, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acacia, and similar others, in such a way that you take any of these things or all together, and mix them with stypic wine or abundantly with honey or vinegar;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and put them on the tooth in a syringe, and hold it tightly, and do not let it out in your hands afterwards;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then remove it, and start another one until the swelling is gone;
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	and you hold steady above a flat piece of stone well made;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	for the property of stone is that it removes all swelling from above the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if its dislocation has already become hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then the cover above, and make the excess apparent;
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	or you cut it with any knife until it is removed, and the care until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains after the limbs are weak and delicate, for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	For because there were too many ligaments, and it could not come to the member's movements.
ou por multitude d’arosement;	For due to the multitude of swelling.
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	For due to too great movements, not in its hour.
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	For because it has little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the cure is that you make the hairs lie down, and make the body tense, until the blood is not multiplied in it.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and give it a bath, and give it joy and ease.
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	Then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts to the great movement, and the swelling often of sharp pain, until the movement corrects the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a dislocated limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the member is misshapen, nevertheless, it does not lose its original work.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	If one does not believe the people who say that one must break the member entirely in two, and many have done this in our land;
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and these works are condemned, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps the death of the patient.
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	Nevertheless, if the dislocations and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they be warmed with hot water, or mollifying herbs be boiled, such as valerian, and roots, and meadowsweet, and similar things;
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and the physician applies a softening plaster, such as fresh lime, and takes the muscle of the shoulder, and cooks it with goose fat or castor oil, and makes a plaster on top.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	and takes figs fat, and grinds them with flax seed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is it necessary to apply continuous and prolonged pressure with wet hands on a dislocation.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And you should allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	And if the distortion is awakened and hardened, like stone, and there is a need to remove it with iron, so that it covers the bone, at the incision slightly subtle.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and place a bandage and apply pressure in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned to its proper place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if it is delayed, the shoulder swells, and if by chance it is reset, it may become stiff.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	Therefore, it is not advisable to move the shoulder when it is swollen:
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	many times causing pain and other injuries.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	Anyway, when it happens, if the dislocation is corrected, then let it rest until the inflammation is calmed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each member as it will heal in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from the elbow to the fingers.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	It is rare that the mandibles are dislocated downwards, and the dislocation of both jaws occurs in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	ou they are a little bit hardened from their heads, and softened a little bit;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are entirely dislocated, and hang downwards, and the saliva from the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its place in many positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entirely and complete, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the minister wets the head of the painful part, and pushes the finger slightly from one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts;
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two fingers should be missing, for it to be even.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instruct the patient to let the jaws relax, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers push evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if it is grinding, immediately if they are both lower jaws together, then apply hot and oily cloths, until it is slightly loosened.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	do not wait too long to reset it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are reset evenly, and the mouth of the patient is closed to soften it, then put on moistened cloths made of a red wax and wax, then tie it lightly with soft bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and let the dislocated limb rest on its back, and its joints should be between two blankets, so that it does not move to the right or left, nor does it try to move, but take light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are closed;
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then feed him what he wants lightly, and does not try to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well closed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper place within an hour and are not converted to their original position, then fevers and sweating become customary, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then cut it off, as it is fatal;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and many times those who have it die in seven days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot be used from the side without continuing to the other side and the worst part, and it is not reset once dislocated, and it is well felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And for the restoration, it is such that the hairs lie quietly on their backs, and extend their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	then press the limb firmly to your palm, and it will return;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then place the poultice and bandage, and hold it in place;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the one who is behind the neck cannot evacuate;
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if not, and if it ever evacuates, then reset it as we have said;
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place the poultice and bandage, hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until he is healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus the dislocated shoulder is returned to its place, when it is separated from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	There are three ways in which the shoulder is not dislocated:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	because one way is that it dislocates to the side of the shoulder blade.
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the back of the shoulder.
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and sometimes dislocates above, and this happens rarely.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and it often dislocates to the side of the shoulder blade, especially those who have little fat, because to these it dislocates easily.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	To those who have enough courage, he leaps forward, and returns forward.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men, a blow or a fracture, and the shoulder swells with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	Therefore, you must first test him until you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	Then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And it is known that a dislocation occurs when it is pulled down towards the shoulder, and it differs between the injured shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a clear difference.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	And you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and desoz from the shoulder to the toucher the top of the shoulder, as if it were an elbow;
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and cannot move his hand to his nose, nor move from any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And thus, if it is dislocated at the top, it is not hidden, for you can see it clearly in the touch.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation is only to be used when it is new, or if the joint is injured.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the caregiver lightly grasps the injured joint at the top, then places their fingers outside the socket, and forces the joint back into place from above.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	And the caregiver lightly grasps and extends their hand, then places it outside.
si venra hastanment.	If it comes out quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come out as we have said earlier, then it is necessary to soak the injured joint in hot, acidic water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and the softening and soothing ointment, such as the decoction of mallow and fenugreek and melilot in vinegar, and it is applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the hairs are shaved over their back, and a cloth strip of equal length is placed under the shoulder, not too thick or too thin, then the patient's foot is placed on the strip, and the shoulder is gently lifted, and the hand of the patient is pulled.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other assistants shave the head of the patient, so that it does not move down.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	that shoulder is now whole, and if you see if the reset is done in this way:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and you must make sure to have someone who is bigger than the pain.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and should be on the side of the chest, and below the shoulder away from the pain, and lift the shoulder high, so that the pain hangs in the arm.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other assistants pull the hand towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the pain is too light, it can move with anything heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also reset in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and it is that you place a long stick in the ground, which the patient should also hold like a staff, and not too heavy or rough.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then it should be placed away from the pain, but with soft cloth above, and the pain should be on the long end of the stick.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then extend your hand to the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	And if it does not return for all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	Take a bandage of two arms in width and four fingers in length, which has the head bent to allow it to enter into the opening behind the shoulder, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	Then tie it above the head with a soft cloth that does not cause pain to the injury, then remove it from behind the shoulder.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	Extend the arm above the cloth, and tie the injury with the cloth, and the arm at the top of the hand, then place the arm over one of the blades of a pair of scissors, and extend the hand below, and let the body hang on the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	The joint is still present now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in any way, it is necessary to place a soft cloth under the shoulder, then apply the plaster evenly with powder from the mill, with incense and a little honey, over the entire shoulder and around, then remove it from under the shoulder gradually, and return the limb to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is better that he move little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	Then move more after three or four days, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And if it is stiff and not made flexible, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is strong from moisture that has come, or for another reason, then it is necessary to administer cautery at three points, as it is placed in front or in the chapter of cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot be raised to the shoulder, then cut the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And cut that the joint will never again fit in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is behind the shoulder and the buttocks, or behind, is caused by impact and stretching of the hands, and there is another remedy administered.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and it is treated until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member becomes stiff and does not move, then use the hairs many times in a bath until that stiffness is relieved and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	That the joint that hurts at the point is dislocated and returns.
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	And it has been dislocated from all parts, and simultaneously in front and behind, and the dislocation is not yet healed, because one can see it well and feel it well.
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	And it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with its healthy counterpart, ensure the patient can see clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is sore, and it cannot bear the weight of the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as the pain comes, because if the pain comes and goes, it would be painful to reset.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	And by chance it cannot be reset entirely, especially when it is at the back.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	It is worse than other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and sometimes it kills the patient.
